<div id="page-1134129">
<h3><a name="page-1134129">Trustees Records, Vol. 4, 1865 (page 067)</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p>67</p>
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title=' Trustees - May 7, 1866 '> Trustees - May 7, 1866 </span><span class='line-break'> </span>The regular monthly meeting of the Trustees was<span class='line-break'> </span>held on Monday May 7<sup>th</sup> 1866, at 10 o'clock<span class='line-break'> </span>a.m. _</p>
<p>There were present the President, and<span class='line-break'> </span>Messrs Adams, Austin, Cheever, Livermore,<span class='line-break'> </span>Norcross and Rand. _</p>
<p>The record of the last meeting was read. _</p>
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title=' Report of Committee on Salaries _ '> Report of Committee on Salaries _ </span><span class='line-break'> </span>Mr Rand for the Committee on Salaries submitted<span class='line-break'> </span>their report as follows: _</p>
<p>"The Committee appointed<span class='line-break'> </span>"to inquire and report upon the compensation of<span class='line-break'> </span>all salaried officers of the Corporation" to whom<span class='line-break'> </span>their Report made April 2, 1866, was recommitted,<span class='line-break'> </span>beg leave to report: _</p>
<p>That upon further consideration, they recommend<span class='line-break'> </span>that the salary of the Secretary be for the present<span class='line-break'> </span>year thirteen hundred and fifty dollars ($1350):<span class='line-break'> </span>and that of the Gatekeeper, six hundred &amp; fifty dollars ($650),<span class='line-break'> </span>with the usual allowance for Sundays.</p>
<p>The Committee are induced to recommend<span class='line-break'> </span>this increase to the amount mentioned in their<span class='line-break'> </span>former report, on account of the present high cost<span class='line-break'> </span>of living and as a special and temporary increase,<span class='line-break'> </span>and not in any way fixing the salaries for any<span class='line-break'> </span>future years. The Committee see no reason for changing <span class='line-break'> </span><small>the salaries of the Superintendent &amp; Treasurer from those mentioned</small><span class='line-break'> </span>in their former Report.</p>
<p><table class='tabular'><thead><span class='line-break'> </span><tr><th>___</th> <th>Edward S. Rand</th> <th>} Committee.<span class='line-break'> </span></th></tr></thead> <tbody> <tr><td>May 7, 1866.</td> <td>Otis Norcross</td> <td>}</td> </tr> </tbody> </table></p>
</div>
</div>
<br />
<div id="page-1134130">
<h3><a name="page-1134130">Trustees Records, Vol. 4, 1865 (page 068)</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p>68</p>
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title=' Trustees - May 7, 1866 _ '> Trustees - May 7, 1866 _ </span><span class='line-break'> </span>The Report was accepted.</p>
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title=' Annual Salaries of Officers established _'> Annual Salaries of Officers established _</span><span class='line-break'> </span>Mr Cheever moved to amend the Report so<span class='line-break'> </span>far as the salary of the Superintendent was<span class='line-break'> </span>concerned by substituting two thousand dollars<span class='line-break'> </span>for two thousand two hundred and fifty dollars;<span class='line-break'> </span>but the amendment was lost.</p>
<p>Mr Rand moved the adoption of the report, and<span class='line-break'> </span>that the question be taken in reference to the salary<span class='line-break'> </span>proposed for each officer separately, by yea &amp; nay<span class='line-break'> </span>vote.</p>
<p>The question being taken on each separately, the <span class='line-break'> </span>recommendations of the Committee were adopted by<span class='line-break'> </span>the following votes: _</p>
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title=' For Superintendt $2250 &amp;c '> For Superintend<sup>t</sup> $2250 &amp;c </span><span class='line-break'> </span>For Superintendent _ twenty two hundred &amp; fifty dollars<span class='line-break'> </span>and the use of house _</p>
<p>Messrs Adams, Austin, Bigelow, Livermore, Norcross &amp;<span class='line-break'> </span>Rand voting yea, &amp; Mr Cheever, nay _</p>
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title=' Treasr $1000 _ '> Treas<sup>r</sup> $1000 _ </span><span class='line-break'> </span>For the Treasurer, _ one thousand dollars,<span class='line-break'> </span>all present voting yea:</p>
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title=' Secretary $1350 _ '> Secretary $1350 _ </span> <span class='line-break'> </span>" [For] " [the] Secretary, thirteen hundred &amp; fifty dollars,<span class='line-break'> </span>all present voting yea:</p>
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title=' Gatekeeper $650. &amp;c _'> Gatekeeper $650. &amp;c _</span><span class='line-break'> </span>" [For] " [the] Gatekeeper, six hundred &amp; fifty dollars, &amp;<span class='line-break'> </span>the usual Sunday allowance,<span class='line-break'> </span>all present voting yea. _</p>
</div>
</div>
<br />
<div id="page-1134131">
<h3><a name="page-1134131">Trustees Records, Vol. 4, 1865 (page 069)</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p>69</p>
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title=' Com. on Grounds authorized to Expend $500 in trees, shrubs, &amp;c '> Com. on Grounds authorized to Expend $500 in trees, shrubs, &amp;c </span></p>
<p>On motion of Mr Rand,</p>
<p>Voted that the Committee on Grounds be<span class='line-break'> </span>authorized to expend a sum not exceeding<span class='line-break'> </span>five hundred dollars in renewing and<span class='line-break'> </span>introducing trees, shrubs, plants and flowers<span class='line-break'> </span>during the present year. _</p>
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title=' Communicaton of Supt respecting H.N. Gardner _'> Communicaton of Sup<sup>t</sup> respecting H.N. Gardner _</span><span class='line-break'> </span>A communication from the Superintendent<span class='line-break'> </span>representing Henry N. Gardner of Belmont, who<span class='line-break'> </span>has heretofore assumed the care of lots solicited by<span class='line-break'> </span>him of proprietors - as an unsuitable man to<span class='line-break'> </span>do any work in the Cemetery, was read: _</p>
<p>The Board being satisfied from fact,<span class='line-break'> </span>coming to the knowledge of the Trustees that the<span class='line-break'> </span>Statement of the Superintendent were true: _</p>
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title=' Gardner Excluded from working in the Cem.y '> Gardner Excluded from working in the Cem.y </span><span class='line-break'> </span>On motion of Mr Rand, it was</p>
<p>Voted that the Secretary be instructed not<span class='line-break'> </span>to issue any permit for the employment of<span class='line-break'> </span>Henry N. Gardner on any lot in the Cemetery.</p>
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title=' Communication of John H. Jenks respecting piece of land adjoining his lot, 1845 _'> Communication of John H. Jenks respecting piece of land adjoining his lot, 1845 _</span><span class='line-break'> </span>A communication from Mr John H. Jenks,<span class='line-break'> </span>proprietor of lot numbered 1845, representing that a <span class='line-break'> </span>small triangular piece of ground contiguous to his lot<span class='line-break'> </span>to which he claimed as belonging to said lot, but which<span class='line-break'> </span>he had never designated with boundary posts, had been<span class='line-break'> </span>sold as lot numbered 3276 to M.B. Markham _<span class='line-break'> </span>was referred to the Committee on Lots with full<span class='line-break'> </span>power. _</p>
</div>
</div>

<h3><a name="page-1134134">Trustees Records, Vol. 4, 1865 (page 072)</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">

<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title=' Trustees _ June 4, 1866 '> Trustees _ June 4, 1866 </span></p>
<p>The regular monthly meeting of the Trustees was<span class='line-break'> </span>held on Monday, June 4<sup>th</sup> 1866, at 10 o'clock a.m.</p>
<p>There were present Messrs Austin, Cheever,<span class='line-break'> </span>Livermore, Lovejoy, Norcross, Rand and Read.</p>
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title=' Chairman pro tem. '> Chairman pro tem. </span><span class='line-break'> </span>The President being absent, Mr Read was<span class='line-break'> </span>chosen Chairman pro tem.</p>
<p>The record of the last meeting was read. _</p>

<div id="page-1134137">
<h3><a name="page-1134137">Trustees Records, Vol. 4, 1865 (page 075)</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p>75</p>
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title=' Amendts to By Law _ Art V. Secretary – '> Amend<sup>ts</sup> to By Law _ Art V. Secretary – </span><span class='line-break'> </span>Mr. Norcross proposed the following amendments<span class='line-break'> </span>to the By-laws: which lie over to the next meeting.</p>
<p>On page 4 of the by-laws (as a few copies have been<span class='line-break'> </span>printed,) Art V. middle of page, in substitution for the<span class='line-break'> </span>present provision for compensation to the Secretary, _</p>
<p>"The Secretary shall receive such salary as<span class='line-break'> </span>the Trustees may vote; and shall account for<span class='line-break'> </span>or pay to the Treasurer all fees received by him."</p>
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title=' [Amendts to By Law _ ] Art VI. Treasurer _ '> [Amend<sup>ts</sup> to By Law _ ] Art VI. Treasurer _ </span><span class='line-break'> </span>Page 5, middle, Art VI: in substitution for the<span class='line-break'> </span>present provision for paying the Treasurer, _</p>
<p>"The compensation of the Treasurer shall<span class='line-break'> </span>consist in a salary to be fixed annually by the<span class='line-break'> </span>Trustees."</p>
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title=' Representatives designated to lots '> Representatives designated to lots </span><span class='line-break'> </span>Upon the petition of the parties in interest, repre<span class='line-break'></span>sentatives were designated for the several lots in con<span class='line-break'></span>nection with which they are named, as follows:</p>
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title=' 8 '> 8 </span><span class='line-break'> </span>James F. Stone of Watertown, son of Melinda Stone,<span class='line-break'> </span>dec<sup>d</sup> prop<sup>r</sup> of lot  numbered 8;</p>

<div class="page-content">
<p>77</p>
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title=' 2385 '> 2385 </span><span class='line-break'> </span>James M. Perkins of Boston, son of Mary<span class='line-break'> </span>Perkins, dec<sup>d</sup> prop<sup>r</sup> of lot numbered 2385;</p>
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title=' 3627 '> 3627 </span><span class='line-break'> </span>Francis Jaques of Charlestown, one of the Trustees under will<span class='line-break'> </span>of Charles Merriam, jointly seized of lot numbered 3627;<span class='line-break'> </span><table class='tabular'><thead><span class='line-break'> </span><tr><th>___</th> <th>Adjourned<span class='line-break'> </span></th></tr></thead> <tbody> <tr><td>___</td> <td>___</td> <td>Attest Austin J. Coolidge, Sec.y</td> </tr> </tbody> </table> <span class='line-break'> </span>------------------------</p>
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title=' Trustees _ Special Meeting _ June 20, 1866. '> Trustees _ Special Meeting _ June 20, 1866. </span></p>
<p>A Special Meeting of the Trustees was holden<span class='line-break'> </span>on Wednesday June 20, 1866, at 10 o'clock a.m.</p>
<p>There were present the President and Messrs Adams,<span class='line-break'> </span>Austin, Little, Lovejoy, Norcross, Rand and Read.</p>
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title=' Subject of Notice to visitors referred to Com. on Grounds _ with power to Employ police _ &amp;c _'> Subject of Notice to visitors referred to Com. on Grounds _ with power to Employ police _ &amp;c _</span></p>
<p>The President stated that he had called the<span class='line-break'> </span>meeting at the suggestion of the Committee on Grounds,<span class='line-break'> </span>on account of a certain "notice to visitors" put up by the<span class='line-break'> </span>Superintendent, in the Cemetery, to which much objection<span class='line-break'> </span>was felt as not suited to the character of the place.</p>
<p>After some informed expression of opinion, and the<span class='line-break'> </span>offering and withdrawal of a motion,</p>
<p>upon motion by Mr Norcross, it was</p>
<p>Voted that the subject be referred to the Com<span class='line-break'></span>mittee on Grounds, with full power, and that they give<span class='line-break'> </span>such notice to visitors, and employ such police force<span class='line-break'> </span>as they may think proper, and report their doings at the next<span class='line-break'> </span>meeting of this Board. <span class='line-break'> </span><table class='tabular'><thead><span class='line-break'> </span><tr><th>___</th> <th>Adjourned<span class='line-break'> </span></th></tr></thead> <tbody> <tr><td>___</td> <td>___</td> <td>Attest Austin J. Coolidge, Sec.y</td> </tr> </tbody> </table></p>
</div>
</div>
<br />
<div id="page-1134140">

<p>At the time for the regular meeting of the Trustees<span class='line-break'> </span>on Monday July 2<sup>d</sup> 1866, at 10 o'clock a.m.<span class='line-break'> </span>there were present the President, and Messrs<span class='line-break'> </span>Cheever, Livermore and Norcross. _</p>
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title=' No Quorum _'> No Quorum _</span><span class='line-break'> </span>There being no quorum present the meeting<span class='line-break'> </span>was adjourned. _</p>

<p>----------------------</p>
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title=' Trustees August, 6, 1866. '> Trustees August, 6, 1866. </span><span class='line-break'> </span>At the time for the regular meeting of the Trustees<span class='line-break'> </span>on Monday August 6<sup>th</sup> 1866, at 10 o'clock a.m.<span class='line-break'> </span>there were present the President and Messrs Cheever<span class='line-break'> </span>and Read. _</p>
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title=' No Quorum _ '> No Quorum _ </span><span class='line-break'> </span>There being no quorum present, the<span class='line-break'> </span>meeting was adjourned. _</p>
<p>Attest Austin J. Coolidge Sec.y</p>
<p>----------------------</p>
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title=' Trustees - September 3, 1866. '> Trustees - September 3, 1866. </span><span class='line-break'> </span>The regular monthly meeting of the Trustees<span class='line-break'> </span>was held on Monday, September 3<sup>d</sup>, 1866, at 10<span class='line-break'> </span>o'clock a.m. _</p>
<p>There were present the President, and Messrs<span class='line-break'> </span>Bowditch, Cheever, Livermore, Lovejoy, Norcross,<span class='line-break'> </span>and Read.</p>
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title=' Notice to Trespassers _'> Notice to Trespassers _</span></p>
<p>The President for the Committee on Grounds<span class='line-break'> </span>reported that the Committee had caused certain<span class='line-break'> </span>notices cautioning visitors not to trespass upon lots<span class='line-break'> </span>to be posted up in different places in the Cemetery,<span class='line-break'> </span>which it was believed would be effectual to remedy<span class='line-break'> </span>the evil complained of.<span class='line-break'> </span></p>
</div>
</div>
<br />
<div id="page-1134141">
<h3><a name="page-1134141">Trustees Records, Vol. 4, 1865 (page 079)</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p>79</p>
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title=' Amendt to By-laws _'> Amend<sup>t</sup> to By-laws _</span><span class='line-break'> </span>Upon motion of Mr Norcross,</p>
<p>It was Voted that the two amendments<span class='line-break'> </span>to the by-laws respecting the compensation of<span class='line-break'> </span>the Secretary and Treasurer, proposed in June,<span class='line-break'> </span>(see p. 75) be hereby adopted. _</p>
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title=' Contract for Perpetual Repair of Lot 2121. '> Contract for Perpetual Repair of Lot 2121. </span><span class='line-break'> </span>The Secretary reported that the Committee on <span class='line-break'> </span>Lots had contracted with the Executors of the<span class='line-break'> </span>late Charles Sanders for the perpetual care of<span class='line-break'> </span>lot numbered no. 2121 for five hundred<span class='line-break'> </span>dollars.</p>
<p>Voted that said contract be hereby concurred<span class='line-break'> </span>in _</p>
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title=' also of Lot 1142 '> also of Lot 1142 </span><span class='line-break'> </span>He also reported that the Committee<span class='line-break'> </span>had contracted for the perpetual repair<span class='line-break'> </span>of lot no. 1142 owned by Sophia M.<span class='line-break'> </span>Cogswell, for the sum of three hundred dollars.</p>
<p>Voted that said contract be concurred in.</p>
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title=' Representn of Lots _ '> Represent<sup>n</sup> of Lots _ </span><span class='line-break'> </span>Upon the petition of the parties in interest represen<span class='line-break'></span>tatives were designated for the several lots in connec<span class='line-break'></span>tion with which they are named, as follows: _</p>

<p>A communication from the Superintendent having <span class='line-break'> </span>been addressed to the Trustees when no quorum was <span class='line-break'> </span>present, requesting the Board to consider the <span class='line-break'> </span>expediency of erecting a house for the propagation of <span class='line-break'> </span>plants, and the same having been informally brought <span class='line-break'> </span>before the Committee on Grounds, the Committee<span class='line-break'> </span>through Mr Read, recommended the following <span class='line-break'> </span>vote: _ which was adopted.</p>
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title='$700 appropriated for plant prop-agating house _'>$700 appropriated for plant prop-agating house _</span><span class='line-break'> </span>That a sum not exceeding seven hundred <span class='line-break'> </span>dollars be hereby appropriated for the erection<span class='line-break'> </span>of a plant propagating house in connection <span class='line-break'> </span>with the flower conservatory.</p>

<h3><a name="page-1134149">Trustees Records, Vol. 4, 1865 (page 087)</a></h3>

<p>87</p>
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title='Lots without permanent numbers, or bounds _'>Lots without permanent numbers, or bounds _</span><span class='line-break'> </span>The Secretary stated that there are many <span class='line-break'> </span>lots in the Cemetery without permanent numbers, <span class='line-break'> </span>some having nothing thereon by which the number <span class='line-break'> </span>is designated, and other having only moveable <span class='line-break'> </span>iron stakes with the numbers cast in iron, which <span class='line-break'> </span>are liable to constant change of location, as well <span class='line-break'> </span>as to be broken off: and he suggested that a gen<span class='line-break'></span>eral examination of all lots in the Cemetery be <span class='line-break'> </span>made with a view to ascertain what lots<span class='line-break'> </span>are so deficient, and that the said lots be <span class='line-break'> </span>numbered at the expense of the proprietors thereof:</p>
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title='The Comee on Lots charged with duty of ascertaining in what cases there is a deficiency _ with full power to cause numbers &amp; bounds to be affixed _'>The Com<sup>ee</sup> on Lots charged with duty of ascertaining in what cases there is a deficiency _ with full power to cause numbers &amp; bounds to be affixed _</span></p>
<p>He also stated that a considerable number of <span class='line-break'> </span>lots are still without permanent bounds. _</p>
<p>It was thereupon</p>
<p>Voted that the <span class='line-break'> </span>duty of ascertaining what lots in the <span class='line-break'> </span>Cemetery are without numbers or bounds<span class='line-break'> </span>be referred to the Committee on Lots with full <span class='line-break'> </span>power to cause all lots to be so numbered<span class='line-break'> </span>and bounded in such manner as they shall <span class='line-break'> </span>deem most expedient. _<span class='line-break'> </span><table class='tabular'><thead><span class='line-break'> </span><tr><th>___</th> <th>Adjourned<span class='line-break'> </span></th></tr></thead> <tbody> <tr><td>___</td> <td>___</td> <td>Attest Austin J. Coolidge</td> </tr> <tr><td>___</td> <td>___</td> <td>___</td> <td>Secretary. </td> </tr> </tbody> </table></p>

<p>91</p>

<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title='Reconveyance of Lot 1594 and new deeds of same in two lots authorized _'>Reconveyance of Lot 1594 and new deeds of same in two lots authorized _</span><span class='line-break'> </span>The Secretary also presented the request of the heirs <span class='line-break'> </span>of the late Martha Lithgow, who was proprietor of lot <span class='line-break'> </span>numbered 1594, containing 600 square feet, repre<span class='line-break'></span>senting that one half of said lot was devised to <span class='line-break'> </span>her daughter Jane Caroline Devens, and the other half to <span class='line-break'> </span>Charles Devens Jr, &amp; Arthur L. Devens as the heirs of <span class='line-break'> </span>Mary Devens dec<sup>d</sup>; and asking leave to reconvey said <span class='line-break'> </span>lot to the Corporation for the purpose of receiving from <span class='line-break'> </span>the Corporation two deeds, each of 300 square feet,<span class='line-break'> </span>one to Thomas M. Devens, son of said Jane C. Devens,<span class='line-break'> </span>&amp; at her request; the other to the heirs of the late Mary <span class='line-break'> </span>Devens (being the said Charles  &amp; Arthur L.)</p>

<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title='Reconveyance of Lots 812 &amp; 817 and new deeds of same, with additl purchase _ in three lots authorized.'>Reconveyance of Lots 812 &amp; 817 and new deeds of same, with addit<sup>l</sup> purchase _ in three lots authorized.</span><span class='line-break'> </span>The Secretary also stated the Application of <span class='line-break'> </span>Henry Lincoln proprietor of lot no. 812 containing 350<span class='line-break'> </span>square feet, and of George Rice, proprietor of lot no. <span class='line-break'> </span>817, containing 350 square feet, for leave to reconvey <span class='line-break'> </span>said lots to the Corporation for the purpose of receiving <span class='line-break'> </span>deeds redividing said land in a different manner <span class='line-break'> </span>between themselves and Mrs Frances M., widow of <span class='line-break'> </span>Henry L. Richardson, who has purchased 80 square feet <span class='line-break'> </span>at the end of their enclosure: _ the new division to be as <span class='line-break'> </span>follows _ Lot No 812 containing 280 square feet to Geo. Rice;<span class='line-break'> </span>Lot 817 containing 260 square feet to Henry Lincoln,<span class='line-break'> </span>and Lot 348 containing 260 square feet to  Frances M.,<span class='line-break'> </span>widow of Henry L. <div id="page-1134154">
<h3><a name="page-1134154">Trustees Records, Vol. 4, 1865 (page 092)</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p>92</p>
<p>Before any action was taken upon either of<span class='line-break'> </span>the foregoing applications, on motion of Mr Rand<span class='line-break'> </span>the following resolution was adopted: _</p>
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title=' New conveyce of lots reconvd to be divided to be only by Quitclaim deed _ '> New convey<sup>ce</sup> of lots reconv<sup>d</sup> to be divided to be only by <u>Quitclaim</u> deed _ </span><span class='line-break'> </span>"That hereafter, whenever a lot shall be con<span class='line-break'></span>veyed to the Corporation for the purpose of dividing<span class='line-break'> </span>or of conveying the same at the request or for the benefit<span class='line-break'> </span>of the party conveying said lot, the new conveyance<span class='line-break'> </span>shall be only by quitclaim deed." _</p>
<p>It was then voted,</p>
<p>That the several applications of the Lithgow heirs,<span class='line-break'> </span>and of Geo. Rice &amp; Henry Lincoln be granted, the<span class='line-break'> </span>new conveyances to be made under the rule<span class='line-break'> </span>just adopted.</p>
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title=' Representation of Lots _'> Representation of Lots _</span><span class='line-break'> </span>Upon the petition of the parties in interest repre<span class='line-break'></span>sentatives were designated for the several lots in<span class='line-break'> </span>connection with which they are named, as follows: _</p>

<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title=' Adjourned Meeting _ Jan.y 28. 1867 _ '> Adjourned Meeting _ Jan.y 28. 1867 _ </span><span class='line-break'> </span>An adjourned meeting of the Trustees was held on<span class='line-break'> </span>Monday, January 28<sup>th</sup>, 1867, at 11 o'clock am.</p>

<p>The record of the last meeting was read. _</p>

<p>Voted that until otherwise ordered,<span class='line-break'> </span>the meetings of the Trustees shall be held<span class='line-break'> </span>monthly, on the second Tuesday of the month,<span class='line-break'> </span>at 10 o'clock a.m. _</p>

<div id="page-1134164">
<h3><a name="page-1134164">Trustees Records, Vol. 4, 1865 (page 102)</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p>102</p>
<p>Mount Auburn Cemetery.</p>
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title='Proprietors Annual Meeting _ Feb.y. 4. 1867 _'>Proprietors Annual Meeting _ Feb.y. 4. 1867 _</span><span class='line-break'> </span>The Annual Meeting of the Proprietors of the <span class='line-break'> </span>Cemetery of Mount Auburn will be held at the <span class='line-break'> </span>Horticultural Hall, Tremont Street, Boston, on <span class='line-break'> </span>Monday, February 4<sup>th</sup> at 3½ o'clock P. M. to <span class='line-break'> </span>to hear the Annual Reports, and choose Trustees <span class='line-break'> </span>for the ensuing year. _</p>
<p>January 28. 1867  Austin J. Coolidge, Secretary.</p>
<p>In accordance with the foregoing notification <span class='line-break'> </span>which was published seven days before the time <span class='line-break'> </span>of meeting in the Boston daily newspapers, the <span class='line-break'> </span>Proprietors met at the time and place therein <span class='line-break'> </span>named. _ .</p>
<p>A quorum being in attendance, Dr. Jacob <span class='line-break'> </span>Bigelow, the President, took the Chair.</p>
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title='Record read _ '>Record read _ </span><span class='line-break'> </span>The record of the last annual meeting<span class='line-break'> </span>was read by the Secretary.</p>
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title='Trustees&apos; Annual Report'>Trustees' Annual Report</span><span class='line-break'> </span>On motion of Jeffrey Richardson Esq. it was</p>
<p>Voted that the reading of the Annual Reports <span class='line-break'> </span>be dispensed with, the same having been distributed<span class='line-break'> </span>among the persons present at the meeting in pamphlet<span class='line-break'> </span>form.</p>
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title='Accepted.'>Accepted.</span><span class='line-break'> </span>On motion also of Mr Richardson it was</p>
<p>Voted that the report of the Trustees be accepted.</p>
</div>
</div>
<br />

<p>He has received for the Fund for Repairs: <span class='line-break'> </span><table class='tabular'><thead><span class='line-break'> </span><tr><th>From New Endowments.</th> <th>4.875.00<span class='line-break'> </span></th></tr></thead> <tbody> <tr><td>" [From] Income of Investments</td> <td>2.569.16</td> </tr> <tr><td>" [From]  Notes Receivable</td> <td>5.300.00</td> </tr> <tr><td>There was in his hands at commencement of yr</td> <td>1.408.42</td> </tr> <tr><td>Balance due the Treasurer</td> <td><u>385.32</u></td> </tr> <tr><td>___</td> <td>___</td> <td>14.537.90</td> </tr> </tbody> </table> <span class='line-break'> </span>He has paid for said account:<span class='line-break'> </span><table class='tabular'><thead><span class='line-break'> </span><tr><th>For care of lots</th> <th>1.156.85<span class='line-break'> </span></th></tr></thead> <tbody> <tr><td>" [For] United States 7-30 Bonds, $3.000 _</td> <td>2.992.05</td> </tr> <tr><td>" [For] <small>" [United] " [States]</small> 5-20 " [Bonds] 10.000 _</td> <td><u>10.389.00</u></td> </tr> <tr><td>___</td> <td>___</td> <td><u>14.537.90</u></td> </tr> </tbody> </table> <span class='line-break'> </span>Boston December 31, 1866  Geo. W<sup>m</sup> Bond, Treasurer _</p>
<p>This certifies that we have examined the books and <span class='line-break'> </span>accounts of the Treasurer of the Proprietors of the Cemetery of Mount <span class='line-break'> </span>Auburn, for the year ending December 31. 1866, and have found them <span class='line-break'> </span>correctly kept and properly balanced, with satisfactory vouchers<span class='line-break'> </span>for all payments charged.</p>
<p>The Certificates of Stocks and other evidences of property <span class='line-break'> </span>were found in accordance with the statement in his accounts.</p>
<p>In the Fund for Repairs there appears to be a balance of <span class='line-break'> </span>$385.32, and in the General Account a balance of $2.877.73,<span class='line-break'> </span>both of which sums appear to be due to the Treasurer. _</p>
<p>Jacob Sleeper, Finance Committee<span class='line-break'> </span>Boston, January 29. 1867.</p>

<div id="page-1134169">
<h3><a name="page-1134169">Trustees Records, Vol. 4, 1865 (page 107)</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p>107</p>
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title='Trustees _ Feb.y 12. 1867 _ '>Trustees _ Feb.y 12. 1867 _ </span><span class='line-break'> </span><u>Trustees Records. 1867-8</u></p>
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title='Meeting for Organization _'>Meeting for Organization _</span><span class='line-break'> </span>The first meeting of the Trustees for organi<span class='line-break'></span>zation and business, which was also the regular <span class='line-break'> </span>monthly meeting, was held at the office of the <span class='line-break'> </span>Corporation (at No. 33 School Street) on Tuesday, <span class='line-break'> </span>February 12<sup>th</sup> 1867. at 10 o'clock a.m. _</p>
<p>There were present Messrs Austin, Bowditch, <span class='line-break'> </span>Cheever, Livermore, Norcross, Rand and <span class='line-break'> </span>subsequently Mr Read. 7 _</p>
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title='Chairman pro tem _'>Chairman pro tem _</span><span class='line-break'> </span>The President being absent, it was</p>
<p>Voted that Mr Norcross be Chairman <span class='line-break'> </span>pro tempore.</p>
<p>The record of the last meeting of the  Trustees,<span class='line-break'> </span>and of the Annual Meeting of the Proprietors <span class='line-break'> </span>was read. _</p>
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title='Ballot for Officers and Committees.'>Ballot for Officers and Committees.</span><span class='line-break'> </span>The Board then proceeded to the choice of <span class='line-break'> </span>the officers and Committees by ballot, and they <span class='line-break'> </span>were declared to be unanimously chosen as follows:</p>
<p>For President  Dr. Jacob Bigelow</p>
<p>For Secretary  Austin J. Coolidge</p>
<p>For Treasurer  George W<sup>m</sup> Bond</p>
</div>
</div>

<h3><a name="page-1134171">Trustees Records, Vol. 4, 1865 (page 109)</a></h3>

<p>109</p>
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title='Treasurer $1000 _'>Treasurer $1000 _</span><span class='line-break'> </span>On motion of Mr Rand,</p>
<p>Voted that the salary of the Treasurer be one <span class='line-break'> </span>thousand dollars for the present year, in full of <span class='line-break'> </span>all services. ($1000.)</p>
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title='Superintendt $2250 &amp; house-rent &amp;c _'>Superintend<sup>t</sup> $2250 &amp; house-rent &amp;c _</span><span class='line-break'> </span>On motion of Mr Rand,</p>
<p>Voted that the salary of the Superintendent be <span class='line-break'> </span>twenty two hundred and fifty dollars, the use of <span class='line-break'> </span>the house, and such wood as he needs for his <span class='line-break'> </span>own use gathered from the premises. _ ($2250 &amp;<s>)</s>c)</p>
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title='Gatekeeper $650 and Sunday allowance.'>Gatekeeper $650 and Sunday allowance.</span><span class='line-break'> </span>On motion of Mr Livermore,</p>
<p>Voted that the salary of the Gatekeeper be six<span class='line-break'> </span>hundred and fifty dollars, and the usual Sunday <span class='line-break'> </span>allowance provided in the by-laws. _ ($650 &amp;c)</p>
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title='Comee to defend vs Grantite Raily rechosen-'>Com<sup>ee</sup> to defend vs Grantite Rail<sup>y</sup> rechosen-</span><span class='line-break'> </span>On motion of Mr Bowditch,</p>

<p>110</p>

<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title=' Lease for 10 yrs. to A.McDonald. approved _ [Lease Expires Jan.y 1, 1877]'> Lease for 10 yrs. to A.M<sup>c</sup>Donald. approved _ [Lease Expires Jan.y 1, 1877]</span><span class='line-break'> </span><u>Voted.</u> "That the Indenture of lease between<span class='line-break'> </span>this Corporation and Alexander M<sup>c</sup>Donald<span class='line-break'> </span>for the term of ten years, for the purpose of manu<span class='line-break'></span>facturing, exhibiting and selling statuary, monumental<span class='line-break'> </span>and other marble or stone work, for Cemetery pur<span class='line-break'></span>poses, which has been submitted by the Committee<span class='line-break'> </span>to whom the subject was specially referred, be and<span class='line-break'> </span>is hereby approved and confirmed, and that the<span class='line-break'> </span>same be executed on the part of the Corporation by<span class='line-break'> </span>the Treasurer and Secretary in the usual manner."</p>

<p>Adjourned<span class='line-break'> </span>Attest. Austin J. Coolidge, Secretary.</p>

<h3><a name="page-1134173">Trustees Records, Vol. 4, 1865 (page 111)</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p>111</p>
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title=' Trustees - March 12, 1867 _ '> Trustees - March 12, 1867 _ </span><span class='line-break'> </span>The regular monthly meeting of the Trustees<span class='line-break'> </span>was held on Tuesday, March 12<sup>th</sup>, 1867,<span class='line-break'> </span>at 10 o'clock a.m.</p>
<p>There were present the President, and<span class='line-break'> </span>Messrs Adams, Austin, Cheever, Little, Livermore,<span class='line-break'> </span>Lovejoy and Read.</p>
<p>The record of the last meeting was read.</p>
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title=' Report of Com. on Grounds on subject of Warming Chapel _'> Report of Com. on Grounds on subject of Warming Chapel _</span><span class='line-break'> </span>The President as chairman of the Committee on<span class='line-break'> </span>Grounds read a report of the Committee on the subject<span class='line-break'> </span>referred to them at the last meeting, in substance<span class='line-break'> </span>recommending that measures be taken to warm<span class='line-break'> </span>the Chapel for funerals, and indicating what the<span class='line-break'> </span>Committee deemed the most practicable method<span class='line-break'> </span>for so doing.</p>
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title=' Rept accepted _ and Comee on Grounds authorized to Erect Furnace &amp;c _'> Rep<sup>t</sup> accepted _ and Com<sup>ee</sup> on Grounds authorized to Erect Furnace &amp;c _</span><span class='line-break'> </span>On motion of Mr Livermore,</p>
<p>Voted that the blank in the report for the <span class='line-break'> </span>appointment of a Committee to cause the work to be<span class='line-break'> </span>done be filled with "the Committee on Grounds."</p>
<p>The report was then accepted, and the<span class='line-break'> </span>following vote recommended by the Committee<span class='line-break'> </span>(with the blank filled) was adopted: _</p>
<p>"Voted that the Committee on Grounds be<span class='line-break'> </span>appointed with instructions, if they shall deem<span class='line-break'> </span>it expedient, to build a furnace outside of Mount<span class='line-break'> </span></p>
</div>
</div>

<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title=' Comee on Catalogue authorized to print matter in separate form for in-formation of purchasers _ '> Com<sup>ee</sup> on Catalogue authorized to print matter in separate form for in-formation of purchasers _ </span><span class='line-break'> </span>On motion of Mr Read,</p>
<p>Voted that the Committee on the Catalogue<span class='line-break'> </span>be authorized, if they think it expedient, to<span class='line-break'> </span>print, in addition to the edition of the catalogue<span class='line-break'> </span>already ordered, such number of copies of<span class='line-break'> </span>a portion thereof in separate form, together with<span class='line-break'> </span>other matter necessary for the information of people<span class='line-break'> </span>wishing to purchase lots, as they think will<span class='line-break'> </span>be advantageous to the Corporation.</p>
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title=' Treasurer in case of absence authorized _ with consent of Finance Comee to appoint a substitute _ '> Treasurer in case of absence authorized _ with consent of Finance Com<sup>ee</sup> to appoint a substitute _ </span><span class='line-break'> </span>The Treasurer intimated the possibility of his<span class='line-break'> </span>absence from Boston, for a considerable time, and<span class='line-break'> </span>asked if the Board would empower some one<span class='line-break'> </span>to perform his duties.</p>
<p>Whereupon it was<span class='line-break'> </span>Voted that the Treasurer, with the consent of<span class='line-break'> </span>the Committee on Finance, be authorized to<span class='line-break'> </span>appoint a substitute as Treasurer during<span class='line-break'> </span>his absence.</p>

<h3><a name="page-1134176">Trustees Records, Vol. 4, 1865 (page 114)</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p>114</p>
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title=' Trustees - April 9, 1867 _'> Trustees - April 9, 1867 _</span><span class='line-break'> </span>The regular meeting of the Trustees was held<span class='line-break'> </span>on Tuesday April 9<sup>th</sup> 1867, at 10 o'clock, a.m.</p>
<p>There were present, the President, Messrs Adams,<span class='line-break'> </span>Cheever, Livermore, Lovejoy, Norcross,<span class='line-break'> </span>Rand and Read. _</p>
<p>The record of the last meeting was read.</p>
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title=' Application of Proprietors of Lots 1349 &amp; 1350 for leave to reconvey and receive new deeds. '> Application of Proprietors of Lots 1349 &amp; 1350 for leave to reconvey and receive new deeds. </span><span class='line-break'> </span>The Secretary stated the application of Hon. John<span class='line-break'> </span>Lowell, Guardian of the minor heirs of Geo. H. Loring,<span class='line-break'> </span>and of Abby M. Loring, deceased proprietors respectively<span class='line-break'> </span>of lots numbered 1349 and 1350, on Oxalis Path,<span class='line-break'> </span>for leave to reconvey said lots to the Corporation, in order<span class='line-break'> </span>that new deeds may issue in accordance with the following<span class='line-break'> </span>statement, and for the reasons contained therein: _</p>
<p>In the year 1847, contiguous lots numbered 1349<span class='line-break'> </span>and 1350, on Oxalis Path, each containing 300 square feet,<span class='line-break'> </span>were granted respectively to George H. and Abby M. Loring,<span class='line-break'> </span>In the year 1853 (the said George H. having deceased) a grant<span class='line-break'> </span>of 300 square feet was made to the said Abby M. of land<span class='line-break'> </span>additional to said lot 1350, but which was actually separated<span class='line-break'> </span>from said lot by lot 1349. At some uncertain period<span class='line-break'> </span>thereafter, an iron fence appears to have been erected<span class='line-break'> </span>around the whole of said land, including a passage <span class='line-break'> </span>way which had been reserved between said lot numbered<span class='line-break'> </span>1349 and said addition to lot 1350, and a division fence<span class='line-break'> </span>was also erected, which left said addition to lot 1350<span class='line-break'> </span>in an enclosure by itself, together with said passageway</p>
</div>
</div>
<br />
<div id="page-1134177">
<h3><a name="page-1134177">Trustees Records, Vol. 4, 1865 (page 115)</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p>115</p>
<p>which had never been paid for, and which made<span class='line-break'> </span>said additional piece so enclosed measure 425 in<span class='line-break'></span>stead of 300 square feet. At the time when<span class='line-break'> </span>it was ascertained that said 125 feet unpaid<span class='line-break'> </span>for have been enclosed for burial purposes, the<span class='line-break'> </span>original proprietors had deceased, and their only<span class='line-break'> </span>heirs were three minor children of Josiah Quincy<span class='line-break'> </span>Loring, a deceased brother of said proprietors, under<span class='line-break'> </span>the guardianship of Dr. Peter Renton, who was the<span class='line-break'> </span>maternal grandfather of said heirs. The said<span class='line-break'> </span>guardian was requested to pay for said 125 feet<span class='line-break'> </span>of land, and advised that it could be added to said lots:<span class='line-break'> </span>and he did pay for it, but out of his private funds,<span class='line-break'> </span>on the supposition that the could make the same avail<span class='line-break'></span>able to his family use. Before receiving any<span class='line-break'> </span>deed thereof, the said Renton died, and was buried<span class='line-break'> </span>in said separate enclosure, but not on the part<span class='line-break'> </span>thereof purchased by him: and his widow is de<span class='line-break'></span>sirous of receiving a deed of so much of said lot<span class='line-break'> </span>as his northwesterly of a line running between the<span class='line-break'> </span>grave of said Renton and that of the said J. Q.<span class='line-break'> </span>Loring. A plan of said lots filed with the plans<span class='line-break'> </span>of the Corporation (to which reference is herein made)<span class='line-break'> </span>shows that said northwesterly part of said lot contains<span class='line-break'> </span>174 square feet, and that the land southwesterly, in<span class='line-break'> </span>both enclosures, measures 851 square feet, which<span class='line-break'> </span>is ample for the purposes of said heirs.</p>
<p>Whenfore said guardian (who has also applied to the Court<span class='line-break'> </span>for leave to convey) for the purpose of correcting the irregularities</p>
</div>
</div>

<h3><a name="page-1134181">Trustees Records, Vol. 4, 1865 (page 119)</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p>119</p>
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title=' Trustees _ May 14, 1867. '> Trustees _ May 14, 1867. </span><span class='line-break'> </span>The regular meeting of the Trustees was<span class='line-break'> </span>held on Tuesday, May 14<sup>th</sup>, at 10 o'clock am,</p>
<p>There were present Messrs Austin, Bow<span class='line-break'></span>ditch, Cheever, Lovejoy, Norcross<span class='line-break'> </span>and Sleeper. _</p>
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title=' Chairman pro tem. '> Chairman pro tem. </span><span class='line-break'> </span>The President being absent, Mr Norcross<span class='line-break'> </span>was chosen chairman pro tempore.</p>
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title=' Perpet. Repair of Lot 1014. '> Perpet. Repair of Lot 1014. </span><span class='line-break'> </span>The Secretary stated that the Committee<span class='line-break'> </span>on Lots had contracted, subject to the approval<span class='line-break'> </span>of this board, with Henry Gurney, proprietor<span class='line-break'> </span>of lot numbered 1014, for the perpetual<span class='line-break'> </span>care of said lot for the sum of four<span class='line-break'> </span>hundred dollars ($400).</p>
<p>Voted that said contract be concurred in. _</p>
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title=' Application to record transfers of lots no. 708 &amp; 2263 in trust _'> Application to record transfers of lots no. 708 &amp; 2263 in trust _</span><span class='line-break'> </span>The Secretary also presented the application of<span class='line-break'> </span>Herman J. Warner for record of a transfer to him<span class='line-break'> </span>by Dr Geo. Bates, in his lifetime, of lot no. 708,<span class='line-break'> </span>with the ornamental ground adjacent,^<sup>also of lots no. 2263 to Joshua H. Bates, of Cincinnati O.</sup> which deeds<span class='line-break'> </span>contained a special declaration of trust, and which<span class='line-break'> </span>under By law, Art. 16, required the sanction of their<span class='line-break'> </span>Board.</p>
<p>Voted that the Secretary be authorized to record<span class='line-break'> </span>said transfers. _<span class='line-break'> </span></p>
</div>

'> Trustees - June 11, 1867. </span><span class='line-break'> </span>The regular monthly meeting of the Trustees<span class='line-break'> </span>was held on Tuesday, June 11<sup>th</sup> 1867,<span class='line-break'> </span>at 10 o'clock a.m. _</p>

<div id="page-1134188">
<h3><a name="page-1134188">Trustees Records, Vol. 4, 1865 (page 126)</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p>126</p>
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title='Trustees _ July 9. 1867 _'>Trustees _ July 9. 1867 _</span><span class='line-break'> </span>The regular monthly meeting of the Trustees <span class='line-break'> </span>was held on Tuesday, July 9<sup>th</sup> 1867, at 10 o'clock<span class='line-break'> </span>a.m.</p>
<p>There were present the President, Messrs Austin, <span class='line-break'> </span>Bowditch, Cheever, Livermore, Lovejoy, Norcross, <span class='line-break'> </span>Rand, Read and Sleeper. _</p>
<p>The record of the last meeting was read.</p>
<p>A communication from the Superintendent <span class='line-break'> </span>represented the expediency of increasing the prices<span class='line-break'> </span>for brick graves and graves in the public lots.</p>
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title='Price of Brick Grave and Int. $25'>Price of Brick Grave and Int. $25</span><span class='line-break'> </span>Voted that the price of a brick grave with <span class='line-break'> </span>the interment shall be twenty five dollars ($25.)</p>
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title='Grave &amp; Int. in Public Lot to be $30.'>Grave &amp; Int. in Public Lot to be $30.</span><span class='line-break'> </span>Voted that the price of a grave in any pub<span class='line-break'></span>lic lot together with the interment shall be <span class='line-break'> </span>thirty dollars ($30.)</p>
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title='Subject of obtaining new location of Office for Trustees &amp; Sec.y refd to Specl Comee _ with full power _'>Subject of obtaining new location of Office for Trustees &amp; Sec.y ref<sup>d</sup> to Spec<sup>l</sup> Com<sup>ee</sup> _ with full power _</span><span class='line-break'> </span>Some discusson was had informally upon<span class='line-break'> </span>practicability of removing the office of the <span class='line-break'> </span>Trustees and Secretary to a new locality where<span class='line-break'> </span>a lease couldbe obtained: _ and it was</p>
<p>Voted that Messrs Rand and Livermore <span class='line-break'> </span>be a committee with full power to arrange <span class='line-break'> </span>for such removal.</p>
</div>
</div>
<br />
<div id="page-1134189">
<h3><a name="page-1134189">Trustees Records, Vol. 4, 1865 (page 127)</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p>127</p>
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title='Supply of Water for Cem.y refd to Specl Comee to report _'>Supply of Water for Cem.y ref<sup>d</sup> to Spec<sup>l</sup> Com<sup>ee</sup> to report _</span><span class='line-break'> </span>Voted that the subject of any arrangement <span class='line-break'> </span>with the Cambridge Water Works for a supply <span class='line-break'> </span>of water for the Cemetery be referred to <span class='line-break'> </span><table class='tabular'><thead><span class='line-break'> </span><tr><th>___</th> <th>Messrs</th> <th>Livermore<span class='line-break'> </span></th></tr></thead> <tbody> <tr><td>___</td> <td>___</td> <td>&amp; Cheever</td> </tr> </tbody> </table> to inquire &amp; report thereon at the next meeting.</p>
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title='Sup.ts Salary increased to $250. _'>Sup.t<sup>s</sup> Salary increased to $250. _</span><span class='line-break'> </span>On motion by Mr Bowditch,</p>
<p>Voted that the Salary of the Superin<span class='line-break'></span>tendent be twenty five hundred dollars _<span class='line-break'> </span>$2500 _ per annum, commencing on the 1<sup>st</sup> of July.</p>
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title='Frank R. Bunker appointed'>Frank R. Bunker appointed</span><span class='line-break'> </span>The Committee on Lots to which was <span class='line-break'> </span>referred in April last the subject of appointing <span class='line-break'> </span>a Gatekeeper with power to make such appoint<span class='line-break'></span>ment subject to the concurrence of the Trustees, <span class='line-break'> </span>reported that they had appointed</p>
<p>Frank R. Bunker<span class='line-break'> </span>and it was</p>
<p>Voted that such appointment <span class='line-break'> </span>be confirmed.</p>
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title='Com. on Catalogue report _'>Com. on Catalogue report _</span><span class='line-break'> </span>The Committee on Catalogue and Plans <span class='line-break'> </span>reported through the Chairman Mr Norcross _<span class='line-break'> </span><del>reported</del> that the Catalogue is nearly ready for <span class='line-break'> </span>distribution, and that the engraving of the <span class='line-break'> </span>map of the Cemetery on Stone is also finished,<span class='line-break'> </span>ready for printing.  The Committee recommends<span class='line-break'> </span>the distribution of the catalogue gratuitously</p>
</div>
</div>

<div id="page-1134190">
<h3><a name="page-1134190">Trustees Records, Vol. 4, 1865 (page 128)</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p>128</p>
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title='July 9. 1867'>July 9. 1867</span><span class='line-break'> </span>to proprietors, but inasmuch as the plan <span class='line-break'> </span>had been attended with extraordinary <span class='line-break'> </span>expense they recommended a charge be <span class='line-break'> </span>made for each copy of the plan given out _</p>
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title='Catalogue to be gratuitously distrib. to proprs'>Catalogue to be gratuitously distrib. to prop<sup>rs</sup></span><span class='line-break'> </span>Voted that the catalogue be gratuitously <span class='line-break'> </span>distributed to proprietors of lots. _</p>
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title='Plan to be sold at 50 cts. 1000 copies to be printed.'>Plan to be sold at 50 cts. 1000 copies to be printed.</span><span class='line-break'> </span>Voted that one thousand copies of the <span class='line-break'> </span>plan be printed, and it be sold at fifty <span class='line-break'> </span>cents per copy. _</p>
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title='Bill of A. Meisel, lithographer, refd to the Pret'>Bill of A. Meisel, lithographer, ref<sup>d</sup> to the Pre<sup>t</sup></span><span class='line-break'> </span>The Secretary presented the bill of <span class='line-break'> </span>A. Meisel, for engraving the plan accompa<span class='line-break'></span>nied by a letter explanatory of his charges, <span class='line-break'> </span>which largely exceeded the contract price.</p>
<p>Voted that the bill of A. Meisel for <span class='line-break'> </span>engraving the plan of the Cemetery be referred <span class='line-break'> </span>to the President with full power. _<span class='line-break'> </span><table class='tabular'><thead><span class='line-break'> </span><tr><th>Adjourned</th></tr></thead> <tbody> <tr><td>___</td> <td>Attest</td> </tr> <tr><td>___</td> <td>___</td> <td>Austin J. Coolidge Secretary</td> </tr> </tbody> </table> <span class='line-break'> </span></p>
</div>

<div id="page-1134191">
<h3><a name="page-1134191">Trustees Records, Vol. 4, 1865 (page 129)</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p>129</p>
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title='Trustees _ Aug. 13. 1867'>Trustees _ Aug. 13. 1867</span><span class='line-break'> </span>The regular monthly meeting of the Trustees <span class='line-break'> </span>was held on Tuesday, August 13<sup>th</sup> A. D. 1867,<span class='line-break'> </span>at 10 o'clock, a.m. _</p>
<p>There were present the President and Messrs <span class='line-break'> </span>Adams, Austin, Cheever, Little, Livermore and <span class='line-break'> </span>Read.</p>
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title='Bill of A. Meisel for engraving stone approved _'>Bill of A. Meisel for engraving stone approved _</span><span class='line-break'> </span>The President reported that, having deemed the <span class='line-break'> </span>bill of A. Meisel for engraving the map of the <span class='line-break'> </span>Cemetery reasonable, he had approved the same.</p>
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title='Comee to procure office for Trustees report in part _'>Com<sup>ee</sup> to procure office for Trustees report in part _</span><span class='line-break'> </span>Mr Livermore of the Committee to procure <span class='line-break'> </span>an office for the Trustees reported that the Com<span class='line-break'></span>mittee had made some progress and asked <span class='line-break'> </span>for further time.</p>
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title='Com. to procure supply of water report in part. '>Com. to procure supply of water report in part. </span><span class='line-break'> </span>Mr Livermore for the Committee to ascertain <span class='line-break'> </span>what arrangement, if any, can be made with <span class='line-break'> </span>the Cambridge Water Works to supply water at <span class='line-break'> </span>the Cemetery, reported in part and asked for <span class='line-break'> </span>further time. _</p>
<p>A communication came from the Superintendent <span class='line-break'> </span>respecting the fees for deposit in the Receiving Tomb,<span class='line-break'> </span>recommending the increase of the same to twenty five <span class='line-break'> </span>dollars ($25): _ Also the laying out of a lot for <span class='line-break'> </span>the interment of bodies left in the Receiving Tomb,<span class='line-break'> </span>for an unreasonable length of time.</p>
</div>
</div>
<br />
<div id="page-1134192">
<h3><a name="page-1134192">Trustees Records, Vol. 4, 1865 (page 130)</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p>130</p>
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title='Trustees - Aug. 13. 1867. '>Trustees - Aug. 13. 1867. </span></p>
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title='Receiving Tomb Lot established _'>Receiving Tomb Lot established _</span><span class='line-break'> </span>It was thereupon voted, _</p>
<p>"That the Superintendent be authorized, <span class='line-break'> </span>on removing bodies from the Receiving Tomb,<span class='line-break'> </span>to inter them in a strip of vacant grounds,<span class='line-break'> </span>between Mistletoe Path and the western stockade<span class='line-break'> </span>fence, said strip to be called Receiving Tomb Lot."</p>
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title='Fee for Deposit in Receiving Tomb to be $25.00 17.00 to be refunded.'>Fee for Deposit in Receiving Tomb to be $25.00 17.00 to be refunded.</span><span class='line-break'> </span>Voted _</p>
<p>"That hereafter the fee for a deposit in the <span class='line-break'> </span>Receiving Tomb be twenty five dollars ($25)<span class='line-break'> </span>seventeen dollars ^<sup>($17)</sup> of which shall be returned<span class='line-break'> </span>to the depositor, if the body shall be removed<span class='line-break'> </span>on his account as required by the laws."</p>
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title='Engine _ enlargement of boiler '>Engine _ enlargement of boiler </span><span class='line-break'> </span>Voted _</p>
<p>"That the enlargement of the engine boiler<span class='line-break'> </span>be referred to the Committee on Grounds with <span class='line-break'> </span>full power. " _</p>
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title='Contract for Perpetual Repair of Lot 596 _'>Contract for Perpetual Repair of Lot 596 _</span><span class='line-break'> </span>The Secretary reported that the Committee on <span class='line-break'> </span>Lots had contracted with Mr Charles Torrey, for <span class='line-break'> </span>the perpetual care of lot numbered five hundred <span class='line-break'> </span>and ninety six (596) for the sum of four hundred <span class='line-break'> </span>and twenty five dollars, subject to the approval <span class='line-break'> </span>of this board:<span class='line-break'> </span><table class='tabular'><thead><span class='line-break'> </span><tr><th>and it was Voted</th></tr></thead> <tbody> <tr><td>___</td> <td>That said contract </td> </tr> <tr><td>be hereby ratified. _ </td> </tr> </tbody> </table></p>

Repair of Lot 801 contract affirmed _</span><span class='line-break'> </span>He also reported that, the heirs of <span class='line-break'> </span>the late Susan L. Willard, deceased propri<span class='line-break'></span>etor of lot numbered eight hundred and <span class='line-break'> </span>one, (801) having removed from said <span class='line-break'> </span>lot the monument and iron fence em<span class='line-break'></span>braced within the terms of the contract <span class='line-break'> </span>for the perpetual repair of said lot, the Com<span class='line-break'></span>mittee on Lots had agreed that said con<span class='line-break'></span>tract should bind this Corporation without <span class='line-break'> </span>further consideration, subject to the concur<span class='line-break'></span>rence of this Board.<span class='line-break'> </span><table class='tabular'><thead><span class='line-break'> </span><tr><th>___</th> <th>Voted<span class='line-break'> </span></th></tr></thead> <tbody> <tr><td>___</td> <td>___</td> <td>That said contract </td> </tr> <tr><td>be hereby ratified. </td> </tr> </tbody> </table> <span class='line-break'> </span><span class='depth3' depth='3' title='General per-mit grantd to A. Wentworth &amp; Co, marble wor<span class='line-break'></span>kers, having presented a memorial representing <span class='line-break'> </span>that said firm is abundantly able to respond to <span class='line-break'> </span>this Corporation for any injury or trespass committed<span class='line-break'> </span>in hauling materials into Mount Auburn, or erecting<span class='line-break'> </span>work therein, and is also willing to be so answerable,<span class='line-break'> </span>accompanied with the request that a general li<span class='line-break'></span>cense may be issued to said firm. _</p>

Wentworth &amp; Co.<span class='line-break'> </span>workable at the pleasure of this Board, said firm <span class='line-break'> </span>first giving a proper obligation to save the Corporation harmless.</p>

<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title='Trustees _ Sept. 10. 1867'>Trustees _ Sept. 10. 1867</span><span class='line-break'> </span>The Trustees held the regular monthly <span class='line-break'> </span>meeting on Tuesday, the tenth day of September <span class='line-break'> </span>A. D. 1867, at 10 o'clock a.m. _</p>
<p>There were present the President &amp; Messrs Austin, <span class='line-break'> </span>Bowditch, Cheever, Livermore and Norcross. _</p>
<p>The Secretary read the record of the last meeting.</p>
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title='Teams for-bidden to enter the front gate. '>Teams for-bidden to enter the front gate. </span><span class='line-break'> </span>Voted that hereafter no teams shall enter <span class='line-break'> </span>the front gate at Mont Auburn.</p>
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title='Report of Com. _ to procure office.'>Report of Com. _ to procure office.</span><span class='line-break'> </span>Mr Livermore for the Committee to procure<span class='line-break'> </span>an office for the Trustees reported the following <span class='line-break'> </span>memorandum of agreement: _</p>
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title='To have offices in 2d story front, 16 Pemberton Sq. for 5 or 10 yrs. @$750. per an. also pay, taxes &amp; for water, gas &amp; heating _'>To have offices in 2<sup>d</sup> story front, 16 Pemberton Sq. for 5 or 10 yrs. @$750. per an. also pay, taxes &amp; for water, gas &amp; heating _</span><span class='line-break'> </span>"It is agreed between the Trustees of Mount Auburn <span class='line-break'> </span>and E. Bangs, Trustee, that the former shall have <span class='line-break'> </span>a lease of five, or ten years, at their option, of two <span class='line-break'> </span>rooms in the Second story, front, of 16 Pem<span class='line-break'></span>berton square, at seven hundred and fifty dollars, <span class='line-break'> </span>per annum, they to pay taxes, water rates, gas,<span class='line-break'> </span>and heating, _ possession to be given and lease<span class='line-break'> </span>made as soon as possible. _</p>
<p>Aug. 29. 1867 (signed) E. Bangs, Trustee."</p>
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title='Accepted for 10 yrs. _'>Accepted for 10 yrs. _</span><span class='line-break'> </span>Voted to accept said lease for the term <span class='line-break'> </span>of ten years. _</p>
</div>
</div>

<div id="page-1134195">
<h3><a name="page-1134195">Trustees Records, Vol. 4, 1865 (page 133)</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p>133</p>
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title='Comee author-ized to dispose of safe &amp; fur-niture  &amp; rent _ and to fit new office _'>Com<sup>ee</sup> author-ized to dispose of safe &amp; fur-niture  &amp; rent _ and to fit new office _</span><span class='line-break'> </span>Voted _</p>
<p>That the same Committee has full <span class='line-break'> </span>power to arrange for the disposal of the safe or any <span class='line-break'> </span>furniture of this office, and for the payment of <span class='line-break'> </span>rent to the present landlord:  also to arrange <span class='line-break'> </span>for fitting up the office in Pemberton Square.</p>
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title='Com. on the obtaining of water asked further time _'>Com. on the obtaining of water asked further time _</span><span class='line-break'> </span>Mr Livermore for the Committee to <span class='line-break'> </span>ascertain if any arrangement can be made<span class='line-break'> </span>with the Cambridge Water Works to obtain <span class='line-break'> </span>a supply of water for the Cemetery, asked<span class='line-break'> </span>for further time. _</p>
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title='Proposition to purchase Stone on which the map is engraved _'>Proposition to purchase Stone on which the map is engraved _</span><span class='line-break'> </span>Mr Norcross for the Committee on the cata<span class='line-break'></span>logue stated that A. Meisel, the lithogra<span class='line-break'></span>pher of the Cemetery Map for 1867 is willing to <span class='line-break'> </span>sell the Stone on which the same is engraved: _<span class='line-break'> </span>that on the reverse side is an engraving of <span class='line-break'> </span>the Back-bay Lands belonging to the City; that <span class='line-break'> </span>the price of the stone will be $134.40 _<span class='line-break'> </span>that he is informed that the City authorities are <span class='line-break'> </span>disposed to join in the purchase: and the <span class='line-break'> </span>Committee recomend the Trustees to take action <span class='line-break'> </span>in that behalf. _</p>
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title='Comee authorized to purchase same jointly with City of Boston'>Com<sup>ee</sup> authorized to purchase same jointly with City of Boston</span><span class='line-break'> </span>Voted</p>
<p>That the Committee be authorized to make <span class='line-break'> </span>such purchase on condition that the City of Boston will <span class='line-break'> </span>join in the purchase, and that a proper contract be made <span class='line-break'> </span>for its ownership &amp; possession.  Adjourned</p>
<p>Attest Austin J. Coolidge Sec.y</p>
</div>
</div>

<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title=' Trustees _ Dec. 10, 1867. '> Trustees _ Dec. 10, 1867. </span><span class='line-break'> </span>The regular meeting of the Trustees<span class='line-break'> </span>was held on Tuesday, December 10<sup>th</sup> 1867,<span class='line-break'> </span>at 10 o'clock a.m. _</p>
<p>There were present the President, and<span class='line-break'> </span>Messrs Adams, Cheever, Livermore, Love<span class='line-break'></span>joy, Norcross and Read. _</p>
<p>The record was read. _</p>
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title=' Furnace for heating Chapel completed _'> Furnace for heating Chapel completed _</span><span class='line-break'> </span>The President for the Committee on<span class='line-break'> </span>Grounds reported that a furnace had<span class='line-break'> </span>been constructed outside and northerly from<span class='line-break'> </span>the Chapel for the purpose of heating that<span class='line-break'> </span>building for funerals. _</p>
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title=' Fee of $10 to be charged for use of Chapel _ when heated _'> Fee of $10 to be charged for use of Chapel _ when heated _</span><span class='line-break'> </span>Upon motion of Mr Norcross,</p>
<p>Voted to accept the report _ and that the<span class='line-break'> </span>vote recommended by the Committee _ to wit _<span class='line-break'> </span>"That a charge of ten dollars be made<span class='line-break'> </span>to all parties on whose account the Chapel<span class='line-break'> </span>may be ordered to be heated."</p>
<p>be adopted. _</p>
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title=' Sec.y to give notice that Chapel will be warmed for funerals _'> Sec.y to give notice that Chapel will be warmed for funerals _</span><span class='line-break'> </span>On motion by Mr Livermore,</p>
<p>Voted that the Secretary be authorized<span class='line-break'> </span>to give notice in the papers that means have<span class='line-break'> </span>been provided for warming the Chapel<span class='line-break'> </span>for funerals _ that a charge will be made<span class='line-break'> </span></p>
</div>

<div id="page-1134200">
<h3><a name="page-1134200">Trustees Records, Vol. 4, 1865 (page 138)</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p>138</p>
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title=' Trustees _ Dec. 10, 1867 '> Trustees _ Dec. 10, 1867 </span><span class='line-break'> </span>to meet the Expense; and that a day's notice<span class='line-break'> </span>will be required. _</p>
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title=' Rate of fare in Horse _ Cars to Cemetery _ refd to Comee '> Rate of fare in Horse _ Cars to Cemetery _ ref<sup>d</sup> to Com<sup>ee</sup> </span><span class='line-break'> </span>The President stated that complaint had been<span class='line-break'> </span>made that a higher rate of fare in the Cambridge<span class='line-break'> </span>Horse-Cars had been charged to proprietors and other<span class='line-break'> </span>persons riding to Mount Auburn than on other parts<span class='line-break'> </span>of the road. _</p>
<p>It was therefore voted _</p>
<p>That the subject of said complaint be re<span class='line-break'></span>ferred to Messrs Little and Cheever to report<span class='line-break'> </span>thereon. _</p>
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title=' Complaint of John Harrington _'> Complaint of John Harrington _</span><span class='line-break'> </span>A communication from John Harrington, mar<span class='line-break'></span>ble worker, addressed to the Treasurer, complaining<span class='line-break'> </span>of an overcharge by the Superintendent, on a bill<span class='line-break'> </span>rendered him for work done by the Corporation,<span class='line-break'> </span>was read by the Treasurer, and it was</p>
<p>Voted that the same be referred to the<span class='line-break'> </span>Committee on Lots. _</p>
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title=' Finance Comee authorized to allow Treasr compensation for additional work _'> Finance Com<sup>ee</sup> authorized to allow Treas<sup>r</sup> compensation for additional work _</span><span class='line-break'> </span>The Treasurer stated that he had been com<span class='line-break'></span>pelled, for the greater convenience and security of<span class='line-break'> </span>the Corporation, to adopt a new system of keeping<span class='line-break'> </span>the books, and that the charge had involved him<span class='line-break'> </span>in considerable extra expense, for which he asked<span class='line-break'> </span>compensation.</p>
<p>Voted that the Treasurer's application be<span class='line-break'> </span>referred to the Finance Committee; and that they</p>
</div>

Z. <p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title=' Trustees _ Jan.y 14, 1868 _ at 16 Pemberton Sq. '> Trustees _ Jan.y 14, 1868 _ at 16 Pemberton Sq. </span><span class='line-break'> </span>The regular monthly meeting of the Trustees<span class='line-break'> </span>was held at the new rooms of the Corporation<span class='line-break'> </span>no. 16 Pemberton Square, on Tuesday, January<span class='line-break'> </span>14, 1868, at 10 o'clock a.m. _</p>
<p>There were present the President and Messrs<span class='line-break'> </span>Adams, Austin, Bowditch, Cheever, Little,<span class='line-break'> </span>Livermore, Lovejoy, Norcross, Rand and<span class='line-break'> </span>Read _ 11.</p>

<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title=' Granite Railway Co. _ suit _ '> Granite Railway Co. _ suit _ </span><span class='line-break'> </span>Mr Rand also introduced the subject of the<span class='line-break'> </span>suit of the Granite Railway Company against<span class='line-break'> </span>this Corporation, which was discussed but<span class='line-break'> </span>no action was taken thereon. _</p>
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title=' Trustees&apos; Annual Report. '> Trustees' Annual Report. </span><span class='line-break'> </span>The President read the Annual report<span class='line-break'> </span>of the Trustees, in print, which was accepted,<span class='line-break'> </span>and ordered to be presented at the Annual Meeting.<span class='line-break'> </span></p>

<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title=' Proprietors&apos; Annual Meeting _ Feb.y 3 1868. '> Proprietors' Annual Meeting _ Feb.y 3 1868. </span></p>
<p>Mount Auburn Cemetery</p>
<p>The Annual meeting of the Proprietors of the <span class='line-break'> </span>Cemetery of Mount Auburn will be held at the <span class='line-break'> </span>Horticultural Hall, Tremont Street, Boston, on <span class='line-break'> </span>Monday, February 3<sup>d</sup> at 3½ o'clock, P.M., <span class='line-break'> </span>to hear the annual reports and choose Trustees <span class='line-break'> </span>for the ensuing year.</p>
<p>Austin J. Coolidge, Secretary.</p>
<p>Jany, 25, 1868.</p>
<p>In accordance with the foregoing notification which <span class='line-break'> </span>was published seven days before the time of meeting in <span class='line-break'> </span>the Boston Daily newspapers, the proprietors met <span class='line-break'> </span>at the time and place therein named. _</p>
<p>A quorum being in attendance, Dr Jacob <span class='line-break'> </span>Bigelow, the President, took the Chair.</p>
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title=' Record Read _ '> Record Read _ </span><span class='line-break'> </span>The call for this meeting and the <span class='line-break'> </span>record of the last Annual Meeting were <span class='line-break'> </span>read by the Secretary.</p>
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title=' Annual Reports _'> Annual Reports _</span><span class='line-break'> </span>The Annual reports in printed form <span class='line-break'> </span>having been distributed among the members <span class='line-break'> </span>present _</p>
<p>On Motion of John M<sup>c</sup>Clellan Esq. it was</p>
<p>Voted that the reading of the annual <span class='line-break'> </span>reports be dispersed with.</p>
</div>

<p>Trustees Records ~ 1868-9</p>

<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title=' Trustees _ Organization _ Feb.y 11, 1868 _'> Trustees _ Organization _ Feb.y 11, 1868 _</span><span class='line-break'> </span>The first meeting of the Trustees for organiza<span class='line-break'></span>tion and business, which was also the regular <span class='line-break'> </span>monthly meeting, was held at the Office of the <span class='line-break'> </span>Corporation, No. 16 Pemberton Square, on Tuesday, <span class='line-break'> </span>February 11<sup>th</sup> 1868, at 10 o'clock a.m. _</p>
<p>There were present, Mssrs Adams, Bigelow, <span class='line-break'> </span>Cheever, Little, Livermore, Lovejoy, Rand <span class='line-break'> </span>and Read _ 9 _</p>
<p>Dr. Bigelow occupied the Chair. _</p>
<p>The record of the Annual Meeting of the Propri<span class='line-break'></span>etors and of the last meeting of the Trustees was read.</p>
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title='Ballot for Officers and Committees _'>Ballot for Officers and Committees _</span><span class='line-break'> </span>The Board then proceeded to the choice of <span class='line-break'> </span>the officers and committees, by ballot, and they <span class='line-break'> </span>were declared to be unanimously chosen, and are <span class='line-break'> </span>as follows: _</p>
<p><table class='tabular'><thead><span class='line-break'> </span><tr><th>For President _</th> <th>Dr. Jacob Bigelow<span class='line-break'> </span></th></tr></thead> <tbody> <tr><td>" [For] Secretary _</td> <td>Austin J. Coolidge</td> </tr> <tr><td>" [For] Treasurer _</td> <td>George W<sup>m</sup> Bond</td> </tr> </tbody> </table> <span class='line-break'> </span></p>
</div>
</div>

<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title='Trustees _ Feb.y 11, 1868'>Trustees _ Feb.y 11, 1868</span></p>
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title='Applicn of Sec.y for increase refd to Specl Comee'>Applic<sup>n</sup> of Sec.y for increase ref<sup>d</sup> to Spec<sup>l</sup> Com<sup>ee</sup></span><span class='line-break'> </span>Voted that the application of the Secretary be <span class='line-break'> </span>referred to a committee of three. _<span class='line-break'> </span><table class='tabular'><thead><span class='line-break'> </span><tr><th>The Chair appointed Mssrs</th> <th>{ Livermore<span class='line-break'> </span></th></tr></thead> <tbody> <tr><td>___</td> <td>{ Cheever</td> </tr> <tr><td>___</td> <td>{ &amp; Read</td> </tr> </tbody> </table> as said committee.</p>

<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title='Treasurer $1,000. _'>Treasurer $1,000. _</span><span class='line-break'> </span>That the salary of the Treasurer be one thousand dollars.</p>
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title='Superintendent _ $2,500 &amp;c.'>Superintendent _ $2,500 &amp;c.</span><span class='line-break'> </span>That the salary of the Superintendent be twenty five hundred <span class='line-break'> </span>dollars, the use of house and such wood as he needs <span class='line-break'> </span>for his own use gathered from the premises.</p>
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title='Gatekeeper _ $650 &amp;c.'>Gatekeeper _ $650 &amp;c.</span><span class='line-break'> </span>That the salary of the Gatekeeper be six hundred and <span class='line-break'> </span>fifty dollars, and the usual Sunday allowance pro<span class='line-break'></span>vided in the by-laws.</p>
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title='Time of Adjournt'>Time of Adjourn<sup>t</sup></span><span class='line-break'> </span>Voted _</p>
<p>That when this meeting is adjourned, it be to the next <span class='line-break'> </span>regular meeting _ the 2<sup>d</sup> Tuesday in March. _</p>
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title='Report on petitn of Harriet M. Miles _ for designation of Revd Henry A. Miles'>Report on petit<sup>n</sup> of Harriet M. Miles _ for designation of Rev<sup>d</sup> Henry A. Miles</span></p>
<p>Mr Rand, for the Com<sup>ee</sup> to which was referred <span class='line-break'> </span>the petition of Harriet M. Miles, devisee in trust <span class='line-break'> </span>of lot no. 236, asking that the Rev<sup>d</sup> Henry A Miles of <span class='line-break'> </span>Brookline, who is a part owner, be designated to <span class='line-break'> </span>represent said lot. _<span class='line-break'> </span></p>
