<div id="page-1134281">
<h3><a name="page-1134281">Trustees Records, Vol. 4, 1865 (page 219)</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p>219</p>
<p>adopted, in the manner and form herein after recorded.</p>
<p>Whereas, the Proprietors of the Cemetery of Mount Auburn,<span class='line-break'> </span>at the annual meeting, on the <date when='1869-02-01'>1<sup>st</sup> instant</date>, requested this Board<span class='line-break'> </span>to prepare and report to them, at an adjourned meeting on the <date when='1869-02-15'>15<sup>th</sup><span class='line-break'> </span>inst</date>, an amendment relating to the election of Trustees, and<span class='line-break'> </span>any other amendments to the act of incorporation which they<span class='line-break'> </span>might think necessary and proper; it is</p>
<p>Voted. That the following brief historical statement by the President<span class='line-break'> </span>be submitted to the Proprietors, and the following amend<span class='line-break'></span>-atory act, in five sections, be reported, for their action<span class='line-break'> </span>thereon:</p>
<p>The land of Mount Auburn Cemetery was purchased and<span class='line-break'> </span>dedicated to its present use in the year<date when='1831'> eighteen hundred and<span class='line-break'> </span>thirty one</date>. It was, by several years, the first establishment<span class='line-break'> </span>of the kind in the United States, it has since been imitated,<span class='line-break'> </span>at various times, by nearly all our prominent cities. Since<span class='line-break'> </span>the year <date when='1835'>eighteen hundred and thirty five</date>, its affairs have<span class='line-break'> </span>been managed by a Board of Trustees varying from seven<span class='line-break'> </span>to twelve in number, elected annually by the proprietors, and<span class='line-break'> </span>which, for the last twelve years, has been kept to the maximum<span class='line-break'> </span>number fixed by the charter.</p>
<p>During a period of nearly forty years, the institution and<span class='line-break'> </span>its property have thus been managed successfully and safely.<span class='line-break'> </span>The Cemetery and its funds have been protected, and have yearly<span class='line-break'> </span>increased, and no imputation of neglect or dishonor has fallen<span class='line-break'> </span>upon any Trustee. Several attempts, however, have, at<span class='line-break'> </span></p>
</div>
</div>
<br />
<div id="page-1134282">
<h3><a name="page-1134282">Trustees Records, Vol. 4, 1865 (page 220)</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p>220</p>
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title=' Trustees _ Feby. 6, 1869 _ '> Trustees _ <date when='1869-02-06'>Feby. 6, 1869</date> _ </span></p>
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title=' Report on Amendt of Charter continued _ '> Report on Amend<sup>t</sup> of Charter continued _ </span><span class='line-break'> </span>different times, been unsuccessfully made to supersede the<span class='line-break'> </span>existing board, by a new and less experienced body.</p>
<p>It is apprehended by many proprietors that the funds<span class='line-break'> </span>designed for the preservation and improvement of the Cemetery<span class='line-break'> </span>have now become so large as to tempt the cupidity of improper<span class='line-break'> </span>and irresponsible persons. At the same time the largely<span class='line-break'> </span>increased number of proprietors affords a greater opportunity<span class='line-break'> </span>than heretofore for clandestine and revolutionary movements.</p>
<p>The Trustees, therefore, in obedience to the instructions<span class='line-break'> </span>of the Proprietors, at their annual meeting, report recommend:</p>
<p>That a petition be presented to the Legislature for an<span class='line-break'> </span>amendment to the act of incorporation to the following effect,<span class='line-break'> </span>to wit:</p>
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title=' Act of Amendment _ '> Act of Amendment _ </span><span class='line-break'> </span>____ <b>An Act in addition to an Act to<span class='line-break'> </span>Incorporate the Proprietors of the Cemetery<span class='line-break'> </span>of Mount Auburn.</b> ____</p>
<p>Be it enacted by the Senate and House of Representatives,<span class='line-break'> </span>in General Court assembled and by the authority of the same,<span class='line-break'> </span>as follows:</p>
<p><u>Sect. 1.</u> The authority conferred upon any cemetery corporation<span class='line-break'> </span>organized under the General Statutes (Chap 28. Sec 2)<span class='line-break'> </span>to take and hold so much real and personal estate as<span class='line-break'> </span>may be necessary for the objects of its organization, be<span class='line-break'> </span>and hereby is rested in the Proprietors of the Cemetery<span class='line-break'> </span>of Mount Auburn.</p>
<p><u>Sec 2.</u> No Member of the said corporation shall in his<span class='line-break'> </span>individual right be entitled to more than one vote.<span class='line-break'> </span></p>
</div>
</div>
<br />
<div id="page-1134283">
<h3><a name="page-1134283">Trustees Records, Vol. 4, 1865 (page 221)</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p>221</p>
<p><u>Sect 3.</u> The officers of the said corporation shall consist of twelve<span class='line-break'> </span>Trustees, a Treasurer, Secretary and such other<span class='line-break'> </span>officers as the Trustees may direct. The twelve persons who now<span class='line-break'> </span>constitute the Board of Trustees shall be divided by lot, or<span class='line-break'> </span>otherwise, as they themselves may determine, into six classes of<span class='line-break'> </span>two each; and the persons of the first class shall go out of office<span class='line-break'> </span>on the day of the next annual meeting, or at an adjournment<span class='line-break'> </span>of the same: and the persons of the second, third, fourth, fifth,<span class='line-break'> </span>and sixth classes shall go out of office, respectively, at each<span class='line-break'> </span>succeeding annual election in the years eighteen hundred<span class='line-break'> </span>seventy-one, eighteen hundred seventy-two, eighteen hundred<span class='line-break'> </span>seventy-three, eighteen hundred seventy-four, and eighteen<span class='line-break'> </span>hundred seventy five: and the two trustees who shall be<span class='line-break'> </span>chosen at the annual meeting in eighteen hundred seventy,<span class='line-break'> </span>and in each succeeding year, shall continue in office,<span class='line-break'> </span>respectively, for the term of six years. In case of the death<span class='line-break'> </span>or resignation of any trustee, the vacancy shall be filled<span class='line-break'> </span>by the Proprietors at the next annual meeting succeeding<span class='line-break'> </span>such death or resignation. Nothing contained herein<span class='line-break'> </span>shall prevent any person whose term of office shall have expired<span class='line-break'> </span>from being re=eligible.</p>
<p><u>Sect 4.</u> The Secretary shall give notice of annual and<span class='line-break'> </span>special meeting of said Corporation by sending by<span class='line-break'> </span>mail or otherwise, to each member of the corporation whose place<span class='line-break'> </span>of residence or business shall be known to him, a printed notice<span class='line-break'> </span>thereof, seven days before the time of such meeting, or by public<span class='line-break'></span>-cation of such notice in one or more newspapers printed in<span class='line-break'> </span>Boston, seven days before the time of such meeting - either<span class='line-break'> </span>or both, as the Trustees may direct. At all meetings a</p>
</div>
</div>
<br />
<div id="page-1134284">
<h3><a name="page-1134284">Trustees Records, Vol. 4, 1865 (page 222)</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p>222</p>
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title=' Trustees _ Feby. 6, 1869 '> Trustees _ <date when='1869-02-06'>Feby. 6, 1869</date> </span></p>
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title=' Act of Amendment of Charter _ '> Act of Amendment of Charter _ </span><span class='line-break'> </span>quorum for business shall consist of not less than twenty<span class='line-break'></span>five members.</p>
<p><u>Sect 5.</u> Any parts of Sections two, three four, and<span class='line-break'> </span>five of the Act incorporating "the Proprietors of the<span class='line-break'> </span>Cemetery of Mount Auburn" approved <date when='1835-03-31'>March 31<span class='line-break'> </span>1835</date>, or of any act in addition thereto, which may be<span class='line-break'> </span>inconsistent with the provisions of this act, are hereby<span class='line-break'> </span>repealed.</p>

Coolidge, and made oath that he would faithfully<span class='line-break'> </span>perform the duties of Secretary of ^<sup>the Proprietors of the Cemetery of</sup> Mount Auburn,<span class='line-break'> </span><table class='tabular'><thead><span class='line-break'> </span><tr><th>___</th> <th>Before me</th> <th>Paul Adams<span class='line-break'> </span></th></tr></thead> <tbody> <tr><td>___</td> <td>___</td> <td>Justice of the Peace.</td> </tr> </tbody> </table></p>

<div id="page-1134285">
<h3><a name="page-1134285">Trustees Records, Vol. 4, 1865 (page 223)</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p>223</p>
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title=' Trustees _ Feby. 9, 1869 '> Trustees _ <date when='1869-02-09'>Feby. 9, 1869</date> </span><span class='line-break'> </span>An adjourned meeting of the Trustees was held on Tuesday<span class='line-break'> </span><date when='1869-02-09'>February 9<sup>th</sup> 1869</date> at 10 o'clock AM.</p>
<p>There were present the President, Mess<sup>rs</sup> Adams, Bowditch<span class='line-break'> </span>Cheever, Little, Lovejoy, Read and Sleeper.</p>
<p>The record of the last meeting was read.</p>
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title=' Application of Secretary &amp; Treasurer _ also Gatekeeper for increase of Salary _'> Application of Secretary &amp; Treasurer _ also Gatekeeper for increase of Salary _</span><span class='line-break'> </span>The President stated that a communication had been<span class='line-break'> </span>received from the Secretary and Treasurer, asking for increase<span class='line-break'> </span>of his compensation for the last fiscal year: also for such<span class='line-break'> </span>increase of salary for the present year as should appear just<span class='line-break'> </span>and proper; _ and another communication from the Gatekeeper,<span class='line-break'> </span>asking for an increase of his salary: and he suggested that<span class='line-break'> </span>a special committee should be appointed to take the whole _<span class='line-break'> </span>subject of salaries into consideration and report thereon at<span class='line-break'> </span>the next meeting; and it was</p>
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title=' Referred to Special Comee _ '> Referred to Special Com<sup>ee</sup> _ </span><span class='line-break'> </span>Voted. That a Committee of three be appointed to take the<span class='line-break'> </span>subject of salaries into consideration, and report at<span class='line-break'> </span>the next meeting.</p>
<p>Upon nomination by the chair, Mess<sup>rs</sup> Norcross Bowditch<span class='line-break'> </span>and D<sup>r</sup> Bigelow were so appointed.</p>
<p>Upon request of the member, of the Board, a statement<span class='line-break'> </span>by the Secretary and Treasurer, relating to his salary,<span class='line-break'> </span>was read.<span class='line-break'> </span></p>

<p>On motion of D<sup>r</sup> Winslow Lewis,</p>
<p>Voted. To accept the report of the Trustees without reading;<span class='line-break'> </span>copies of the same having been mailed to the members of<span class='line-break'> </span>the Corporation.</p>
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title=' Suggest Amendments to the Report '> Suggest Amendments to the Report </span><span class='line-break'> </span>William Brigham Esq moved the adoption of the<span class='line-break'> </span>report; pending which, several amendments were proposed. ,</p>
<p>the first by W<sup>m</sup> A Wingate Esq, that the last clause of<span class='line-break'> </span>section third be amended, so that trustees should not be<span class='line-break'> </span>re=eligible until six years after the expiration of their term,</p>
<p>another by J D Braman Esq; that section third be<span class='line-break'> </span>so amended as to divide the board into three classes of four each.<span class='line-break'> </span></p>

<p>There were present, the President, Mess<sup>rs</sup> Adams<span class='line-break'> </span>Bowditch, Cheever, Lovejoy Norcross and Read &amp; Sleeper.</p>

<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title=' Report of Committee on Salaries _ recommending grant to Treasr for last year of $500 _'> Report of Committee on Salaries _ recommending grant to Treas<sup>r</sup> for last year of $500 _</span><span class='line-break'> </span>M<sup>r</sup> Norcross for the Committee on Salaries submitted<span class='line-break'> </span>their report in writing, of which the following is a copy</p>
<p>Office Mount Auburn Cemetery<span class='line-break'> </span>Boston<date when='1869-03-09'> March 9, 1969</date>.</p>
<p>The Committee to whom was referred the<span class='line-break'> </span>communication of the Treasurer in regard to extra labor<span class='line-break'> </span>in his department during the past year _<span class='line-break'> </span>make the following Report</p>
<p>They find by examination and enquiry, that<span class='line-break'> </span>in consequence of the unsatisfactory condition of the books &amp;<span class='line-break'> </span>accounts of the late Treasurer, when they came into the<span class='line-break'> </span>possession of the present officer, an unexpected amount<span class='line-break'> </span>of labor has been required, from both the Treasurer and<span class='line-break'> </span>his assistant, in the adjustment of the accounts &amp; collection<span class='line-break'> </span>of the bills due the corporation. The amount collected from<span class='line-break'> </span>the overdue bills has been quite large, and the books and<span class='line-break'> </span>accounts are assuming a more satisfactory condition.</p>
<p>As this additional labor was not anticipated when the<span class='line-break'> </span></p>
</div>

<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title=' [Report of Committee on Salaries _ recommending grant to Treasr for last year of $500 _] and  for present year addition to salary of $500. and to Gatekeeper&apos;s of $50 _'> [Report of Committee on Salaries _ recommending grant to Treas<sup>r</sup> for last year of $500 _] and  for present year addition to salary of $500. and to Gatekeeper's of $50 _</span><span class='line-break'> </span>Salary of Treasurer was fixed for the past year, the Committee<span class='line-break'> </span>are unanimous in recommending the passage of the following <span class='line-break'> </span>vote.</p>
<p>Voted. That the sum of Five hundred dollars be paid the<span class='line-break'> </span>Treasurer in full compensation for extra labor in<span class='line-break'> </span>his department during the year 1868.</p>
<p>The whole subject of Salaries having been referred<span class='line-break'> </span>to the same Committee _ They beg leave to Report. _</p>
<p>When the office of Treasurer was transferred to<span class='line-break'> </span>the present incumbent, it was supposed that with temporary<span class='line-break'> </span>assistance he could perform the duties of Secretary and<span class='line-break'> </span>Treasurer. The investigations of the Committee have made<span class='line-break'> </span>it apparent that the proper and satisfactory performance of<span class='line-break'> </span>these duties, will require the employment by the Treasurer<span class='line-break'> </span>of a permanent and competent assistant. To enable him<span class='line-break'> </span>to make this arrangement, the committee unanimously<span class='line-break'> </span>recommend the addition of Five hundred dollars to his<span class='line-break'> </span>salary as Treasurer, making the total amount of his<span class='line-break'> </span>salary as Treasurer for 1869 Fifteen hundred dollars,<span class='line-break'> </span>instead of One thousand dollars as originally fixed for<span class='line-break'> </span>1868:</p>
<p>The Committee have also considered the application<span class='line-break'> </span>of the Gate-Keeper for additional compensation. They have<span class='line-break'> </span>ascertained that the has performed his duties acceptably,<span class='line-break'> </span>and is a useful man in that position, and recommend<span class='line-break'> </span>an addition to his salary for 1869 of Fifty dollars, making<span class='line-break'> </span></p>

<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title=' Treasurer&apos;s Quarterly Statement _'> Treasurer's Quarterly Statement _</span><span class='line-break'> </span>The Treasurer submitted his quarterly statement<span class='line-break'> </span>of the condition of the Treasury on the <date when='1869-04-01'>1<sup>st</sup> inst.</date> and a<span class='line-break'> </span>trial balance sheet of the books on said date. _ and the<span class='line-break'> </span>same was referred to the Finance Committee.</p>
<p>The Board ratified the action of the Committee<span class='line-break'> </span>on Lots, in making contracts for perpetual repair of<span class='line-break'> </span>lots in the following cases.</p>

<div id="page-1134300">
<h3><a name="page-1134300">Trustees Records, Vol. 4, 1865 (page 238)</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p>238</p>
<p>An Act</p>
<p>in addition to an act to incorporate the Proprietors of the<span class='line-break'> </span>Cemetery of Mount Auburn.</p>
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title=' Copy of act in addition to act of Incorporation _ '> Copy of act in addition to act of Incorporation _ </span><span class='line-break'> </span>Be it enacted by the Senate and House<span class='line-break'> </span>of Representatives, in General Court assembled, and<span class='line-break'> </span>by the authority of the same as follows: _</p>
<p><u>Section 1.</u> The authority conferred upon any cemetery<span class='line-break'> </span>corporation organized under the provisions of section two,<span class='line-break'> </span>of chapter twenty eight of the General Statutes to take and<span class='line-break'> </span>hold so much real and personal estate as may be necessary<span class='line-break'> </span>for the objects of its organization, is hereby vested in the<span class='line-break'> </span>proprietors of the Cemetery of Mount Auburn.</p>
<p><u>Section 2.</u> No member of said corporation shall in his<span class='line-break'> </span>individual right be entitled to more than one vote at the<span class='line-break'> </span>meetings of said Corporation.</p>
<p><u>Section 3.</u> The officers of said Corporation shall consist<span class='line-break'> </span>of twelve trustees, a treasurer, secretary and such other<span class='line-break'> </span>officers as the trustees may direct. The twelve persons<span class='line-break'> </span>who now constitute the board of trustees shall be divided<span class='line-break'> </span>by lot or otherwise, as they themselves may determine,<span class='line-break'> </span>into six classes of two each; and the persons of the first<span class='line-break'> </span>class shall go out of office on the day of the next _<span class='line-break'> </span>annual meeting; and the persons of the second, third,<span class='line-break'> </span>fourth, fifth and sixth classes shall go out of office,<span class='line-break'> </span>respectively, on the day of each succeeding annual<span class='line-break'> </span>election in the years eighteen hundred and seventy one,<span class='line-break'> </span>eighteen hundred and seventy two, eighteen hundred and <span class='line-break'> </span></p>
</div>
</div>
<br />
<div id="page-1134301">
<h3><a name="page-1134301">Trustees Records, Vol. 4, 1865 (page 239)</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p>239</p>
<p>seventy three, eighteen hundred and seventy four, and<span class='line-break'> </span>eighteen hundred and seventy five; and the two trustees<span class='line-break'> </span>who shall be chosen at the annual meeting in the year<span class='line-break'> </span>eighteen hundred and seventy, and in each succeeding<span class='line-break'> </span>year, shall continue in office, respectively, for the term<span class='line-break'> </span>of six years. In case of the death or resignation of<span class='line-break'> </span>any trustee, the vacancy shall be filled by the proprietors<span class='line-break'> </span>at the next annual meeting succeeding such death or<span class='line-break'> </span>resignation. Nothing herein contained shall prevent<span class='line-break'> </span>any person whose term of office shall have expired from<span class='line-break'> </span>being re-eligible.</p>
<p><u>Section 4.</u> The Secretary shall give notice of annual<span class='line-break'> </span>and special meetings of said corporation by sending by<span class='line-break'> </span>mail or otherwise, to each member of the corporation<span class='line-break'> </span>whose place of residence or business shall be known to<span class='line-break'> </span>him, a printed notice thereof, seven days before the<span class='line-break'> </span>time of such meeting, and by publication of such notice<span class='line-break'> </span>in one or more newspapers printed in Boston, seven<span class='line-break'> </span>days before the time of such meeting, At all meetings<span class='line-break'> </span>a quorum for business shall consist of not less than<span class='line-break'> </span>twenty five members.</p>
<p><u>Section 5. </u> Such parts of sections two, three, four and<span class='line-break'> </span>five of chapter ninety six of the acts of the year<span class='line-break'> </span>eighteen hundred and thirty five, or of any act in<span class='line-break'> </span>addition to which may be inconsistent with the provisions<span class='line-break'> </span>of this act are hereby repealed</p>
<p>House of Representatives. <date when='1869-04-13'>April 13, 1869</date>.<span class='line-break'> </span>Passed to be enacted.</p>
<p>Harvey Jewell, Speaker</p>
</div>
</div>
<br />

<h3><a name="page-1134303">Trustees Records, Vol. 4, 1865 (page 241)</a></h3>

<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title=' Trustees _ Jun 8, 1869. '> Trustees _ <date when='1869-06-08'>Jun 8, 1869</date>. </span><span class='line-break'> </span>The regular meeting of the Trustees was<span class='line-break'> </span>held on Tuesday <date when='1869-06-08'>June 8, 1869</date>, at 10 'oclock AM.</p>
<p>There were present, the President, Mess<sup>rs</sup> Adams,<span class='line-break'> </span>Austin, Bowditch, Cheever, Livermore, Lovejoy, Norcross<span class='line-break'> </span>and Read.</p>
<p>The record of the last meeting was read.</p>
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title=' Report of Com. of Intermts on subject of second Intermts in Public Lots _ '> <small>Report of Com. of Interm<sup>ts</sup> on subject of second Interm<sup>ts</sup> in Public Lots _</small> </span><span class='line-break'> </span>The Committee on Interments submitted a <span class='line-break'> </span>written report on the subject referred to said Committee in<span class='line-break'> </span>August last. viz. as to what charge should be made in<span class='line-break'> </span>cases of second Interments in graves in the Public Lots. _</p>
<p>Recommending that hereafter every where in the<span class='line-break'> </span>Cemetery not more than two interments in the same grave<span class='line-break'> </span>shall be permitted, and that upon a second interment<span class='line-break'> </span>in a grave in a public lot no further charge should be<span class='line-break'> </span>made for land, but the usual interment fee should be<span class='line-break'> </span>collected; and that the by laws should be amended in<span class='line-break'> </span>conformity with this recommendation.</p>
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title=' Adopted _ '> Adopted _ </span><span class='line-break'> </span>The report was accepted and adopted.</p>
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title=' Amendt of By-laws _ Interment. '> Amend<sup>t</sup> of By-laws _ Interment. </span><span class='line-break'> </span>Upon the recommendation of the Committee<span class='line-break'> </span>the following amendments to the 19<sup>th</sup> article of by laws<span class='line-break'> </span>was proposed, and laid upon the table to the next meeting.</p>
<p>Substitute for the clause "Where more than<span class='line-break'> </span>one interment is made in the same grave, the last</p>
</div>
</div>

<div id="page-1134304">
<h3><a name="page-1134304">Trustees Records, Vol. 4, 1865 (page 242)</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p>242</p>
<p>shall be at least three feet below the surface of the ground"<span class='line-break'> </span>the following". Not more than two interments shall<span class='line-break'> </span>be made in the same grave, the latter of which shall<span class='line-break'> </span>be at least three feet below the surface of the ground."</p>
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title=' Drainage of low land near Locust Av _ '> Drainage of low land near Locust Av _ </span><span class='line-break'> </span>The Committee on Lots verbally reported that<span class='line-break'> </span>they had examined the vicinity of lots where proprietors<span class='line-break'> </span>had complained of bad drainage from their lots, but<span class='line-break'> </span>had not come to a decision as to the best means to remove<span class='line-break'> </span>the cause of complaint.</p>
<p>It was then</p>
<p>Voted. To refer the subject of draining certain lots<span class='line-break'> </span>on and near Locust Avenue, to the Committee<span class='line-break'> </span>on Lots: with full power.</p>
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title=' Proposition of A. McDonald to sell marble Shop _ '> Proposition of A. M<sup>c</sup>Donald to sell marble Shop _ </span><span class='line-break'> </span>A written proposition from Alex<sup>r</sup> M<sup>c</sup>Donald<span class='line-break'> </span>offering to sell the building occupied by him as a marble<span class='line-break'> </span>shop on land leased to him by the Corporation for the<span class='line-break'> </span>sum of Four hundred and fifty dollars ($450 _) _<span class='line-break'> </span>was referred to the Committee on Grounds with full <span class='line-break'> </span>power.</p>

<div id="page-1134306">
<h3><a name="page-1134306">Trustees Records, Vol. 4, 1865 (page 244)</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p>244</p>
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title=' Trustees _ July 13, 1869 '> Trustees _ <date when='1869-07-13'>July 13, 1869</date> </span><span class='line-break'> </span>The regular meeting of the Trustees was<span class='line-break'> </span>held on Tuesday <date when='1869-07-13'>July 13 1869</date>, at 10 o'clock AM.</p>
<p>There were present, the President, Mess<sup>rs</sup><span class='line-break'> </span>Austin, Cheever, Lovejoy and Norcross.</p>
<p>The record of the last meeting was read</p>
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title=' Amendt of By-law _ Interment _'> Amend<sup>t</sup> of By-law _ Interment _</span><span class='line-break'> </span>The amendment ot the By laws proposed<span class='line-break'> </span>at the last meeting was read and adopted, and is as<span class='line-break'> </span>follows.</p>
<p>In the 19<sup>th</sup> article, substitute for the clause<span class='line-break'> </span>"Where more than one interment is made in the same<span class='line-break'> </span>grave, the last shall be at least three feet below the<span class='line-break'> </span>surface of the ground," the following. "Not more<span class='line-break'> </span>than two interments shall be made in the same grave,<span class='line-break'> </span>the latter of which shall be at least three feet below the<span class='line-break'> </span>surface of the ground."</p>
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title=' Report on A. McDonald&apos;s proposal to sell marble shop. '> Report on A. M<sup>c</sup>Donald's proposal to sell marble shop. </span><span class='line-break'> </span>The President of the Committee on<span class='line-break'> </span>Grounds reported upon the matter of purchasing the<span class='line-break'> </span>marble shop of A. M<sup>c</sup>Donald referred to them at the<span class='line-break'> </span>meeting of the Board <date when='1869-06-08'>June 8<sup>th</sup> 1869</date>, that M<sup>r</sup> M<sup>c</sup><span class='line-break'> </span>Donald had removed the shop from the ground before<span class='line-break'> </span>action of the Committee, and the Committee there<span class='line-break'></span>-for ask to be discharged from further consideration<span class='line-break'> </span>of the subject.</p>
<p>The report was accepted, and the<span class='line-break'> </span>Committee discharged.</p>
</div>
</div>
<br />
<div id="page-1134307">
<h3><a name="page-1134307">Trustees Records, Vol. 4, 1865 (page 245)</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p>245</p>
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title=' Perpet. Repair of Lot 1794. '> Perpet. Repair of Lot 1794. </span><span class='line-break'> </span>The Committee on Lots reported. That<span class='line-break'> </span>they had contracted with the Trustees of Henry Smith<span class='line-break'> </span>for the perpetual care of Lot N<sup>o</sup> 1794 for four hundred<span class='line-break'> </span>and fifty dollars, and said contract was ratified.</p>
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title=' Treasurer&apos;s Quarterly statement _ '> Treasurer's Quarterly statement _ </span><span class='line-break'> </span>The Treasurer submitted his quarterly state<span class='line-break'></span>-ment, and the same was referred to the Finance<span class='line-break'> </span>Committee, with a request that said Committee should<span class='line-break'> </span>report on same at next meeting of the Board.</p>
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title=' Treasrs Report to be approved by Comee of Finance before presentation _ '> <small>Treas<sup>rs</sup> Report to be approved by Com<sup>ee</sup> of Finance before presentation _</small> </span><span class='line-break'> </span>Voted. That hereafter the report of the Treasurer be<span class='line-break'> </span>submitted to the Committee of Finance for<span class='line-break'> </span>approval, before it shall be presented to this <span class='line-break'> </span>Board.</p>
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title=' Surveyor&apos;s bill _ '> Surveyor's bill _ </span><span class='line-break'> </span>A bill of $448.15 of J H Shedd, for<span class='line-break'> </span>surveying, was referred to Mess<sup>rs</sup> Cheever and<span class='line-break'> </span>Lovejoy, to report thereon at the next meeting.<span class='line-break'> </span><table class='tabular'><thead><span class='line-break'> </span><tr><th>___</th> <th>Adjourned<span class='line-break'> </span></th></tr></thead> <tbody> <tr><td>___</td> <td>___</td> <td>Attest</td> </tr> <tr><td>___</td> <td>Austin J. <p>246</p>
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title='Trustees _ Aug. 10. 1869.'>Trustees _ <date when='1869-08-10'>Aug. 10. 1869</date>.</span><span class='line-break'> </span>The monthly meeting of the Trustees was<span class='line-break'> </span>held on Tuesday <date when='1869-08-10'>August 10<sup>th</sup></date> at 10 o'clock Am</p>
<p>There were present the President and Mess<sup>rs</sup><span class='line-break'> </span>Adams, Austin, Cheever, Lovejoy, Rand &amp; Sleeper _</p>
<p>The record of the last meeting was read and <span class='line-break'> </span>approved.</p>
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title='J. H. Shedd&apos;s Bill for surveying to be paid.'>J. H. Shedd's Bill for surveying to be paid.</span><span class='line-break'> </span>M<sup>r</sup> Cheever for the Committee to which was <span class='line-break'> </span>referred at the last meeting the bill of J H Shedd the <span class='line-break'> </span>surveyer, recommended that the bill be paid.</p>
<p>and it was Voted.  That the Treasurer <span class='line-break'> </span>be authorized to pay the same.</p>
<p>Upon suggestion of the President that <span class='line-break'> </span>complaint is made that the dust from street in front of the <span class='line-break'> </span>Cemetery is very objectionable to proprietors of lots in <span class='line-break'> </span>that vicinity.</p>
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title='Watering Mt. Auburn Street _'>Watering Mt. Auburn Street _</span><span class='line-break'> </span>Upon motion by M<sup>r</sup> Rand it was</p>
<p>Voted.  That a Committee be appointed to consider the <span class='line-break'> </span>most practical mode of watering said street,<span class='line-break'> </span>and report thereon:  and that said Committee<span class='line-break'> </span>also have power to contract with the Railroad <span class='line-break'> </span>Company or any other party for watering said <span class='line-break'> </span>street during the present season.</p>
<p>Upon nomination by the chair M<sup>r</sup> <span class='line-break'> </span>Cheever and M<sup>r</sup> Lovejoy were so appointed.</p>
</div>

<p>After discussion the subject was postponed<span class='line-break'> </span>to the next meeting of the Board.</p>
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title='Resolutions of Respect for Chas. C. Little.'>Resolutions of Respect for Chas. C. Little.</span><span class='line-break'> </span>The following resolutions were then pre<span class='line-break'></span>-sented to the Board, and unanimously adopted.</p>
<p>Whereas the painful intelligence of the <span class='line-break'> </span>removal from life on the<date when='1869-08-09'> 9<sup>th</sup> inst.</date> of one of the oldest <span class='line-break'> </span>members of this board has been announced: _</p>
<p>Be it Resolved that in the death of <span class='line-break'> </span>Charles C. Little, Esquire, whose official connection <span class='line-break'> </span>with the Trustees of the Cemetery of Mount Auburn <span class='line-break'> </span>has continued uninterruptedly for the period <span class='line-break'> </span>of seventeen years, we have to regret the loss of an –</p>
</div>

<div id="page-1134310">
<h3><a name="page-1134310">Trustees Records, Vol. 4, 1865 (page 248)</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p>248</p>
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title='Trustees _ Aug. 10. 1869 _ continued _'>Trustees _ <date when='1869-08-10'>Aug. 10. 1869</date> _ continued _</span><span class='line-break'> </span>associate valued for his modest deportment and thorough<span class='line-break'> </span>business habits.  His kindness of heart and clear<span class='line-break'> </span>sagacity deserved and won the esteem of his co-trustees,<span class='line-break'> </span>and the withdrawal of his ripe experience will be a <span class='line-break'> </span>serious loss.</p>
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title='Resolutions upon decease of Chas. C. Little.'>Resolutions upon decease of Chas. C. Little.</span><span class='line-break'> </span>Resolved, that a copy of this expression of <span class='line-break'> </span>our sentiments be communicated to his afflicted family,<span class='line-break'> </span>with the assurance of our most earnest sympathy in <span class='line-break'> </span>their solemn bereavements and that the same be <span class='line-break'> </span>entered upon the records of this Board.</p>
<p>[strong diagonal line right to left covering eight blank lines]</p>
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title='Paul Adams chosen to fill vacancy on finance Com.'>Paul Adams chosen to fill vacancy on finance Com.</span><span class='line-break'> </span>Mr Sleeper suggested the expediency of <span class='line-break'> </span>filling the vacancy upon the Committee of Finance, occa=<span class='line-break'> </span>-sioned by the death of M<sup>r</sup> Little.</p>
<p>Voted.  To fill said vacancy.</p>
<p>A balloting was had, and Paul Adams <span class='line-break'> </span>was chosen to fill said vacancy.</p>
<p>Adjourned.  Attest</p>
<p>Austing J. Coolidge Secretary.</p>
</div>

<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title='Trustees - Octo. 12. 1869'>Trustees - <date when='1869-10-12'>Octo. 12. 1869</date></span><span class='line-break'> </span>The regular meeting of the Trustees was held <span class='line-break'> </span>on Tuesday<date when='1869-10-12'> October 12 1869</date>. at 10 oclock Am</p>
<p>There were present the President &amp; Mess<sup>rs</sup> Adams:<span class='line-break'> </span>Austin, Bowditch, Cheever, Lovejoy, Rand &amp; Sleeper. . 8 .</p>

<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title='Claim of Landlord for Porterage adjusted _'>Claim of Landlord for Porterage adjusted _</span><span class='line-break'> </span>The Committee of Finance reported in the matter<span class='line-break'> </span>of the claim of porterage referred to said Committee at the <span class='line-break'> </span>last meeting, that the claim had been satisfactorily settled.</p>
<p>The report was accepted.</p>
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title='Abatement of Taxes in Cambridge _ '>Abatement of Taxes in Cambridge _ </span><span class='line-break'> </span>Said Committee also reported in relation to <span class='line-break'> </span>abatement of taxes by the City of Cambridge, that the <span class='line-break'> </span>Treasurer had secured an abatement of $3000. on the <span class='line-break'> </span>valuation of real estate; or $42. on tax bill.</p>
<p>The report was accepted.</p>
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title='Supply Water for Cemetery _'>Supply Water for Cemetery _</span><span class='line-break'> </span>The Committee appointed in relation to a supply<span class='line-break'> </span>of water for watering the street in front of the Cemetery, report<span class='line-break'></span>=ed, that the question had been presented to the Committee in <span class='line-break'> </span>a new form. _ that the persons living on the street between <span class='line-break'> </span>Mount Auburn gate and Fayerweather Street are anxious <span class='line-break'> </span>to obtain a supply of water from the City of Cambridge, <span class='line-break'> </span>and the Cambridge Water Works are ready to lay main pipe<span class='line-break'> </span>between said points, if the abutters will subscribe and pay</p>

<p>252</p>
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title='Trustees _ contind _ Oct. 12. 1869 _'>Trustees _ contin<sup>d</sup> _ <date when='1869-10-12'>Oct. 12. 1869</date> _</span><span class='line-break'> </span>ten per cent of the cost of such laying which is estimated <span class='line-break'> </span>at $319.00; that subscriptions had been obtained from the <span class='line-break'> </span>other abutters, amounting to $200 ~, leaving $119.~ to be <span class='line-break'> </span>provided for in order to obtain the water, which can be <span class='line-break'> </span>used to advantage at the greenhouse, for the water closets, <span class='line-break'> </span>of the proposed new house, and for watering street around<span class='line-break'> </span>the gate.</p>

<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title='Comee of inquiry as to violation of By-law forbidding Officers fo Corpn to have interest in work or materials for Cemetery _'>Com<sup>ee</sup> of inquiry as to violation of By-law forbidding Officers fo Corp<sup>n</sup> to have interest in work or materials for Cemetery _</span><span class='line-break'> </span>On motion of M<sup>r</sup> Cheever; it was</p>
<p>Voted.  That a Committee of three be appointed to examine <span class='line-break'> </span>and report to this Board, whether there has been <span class='line-break'> </span>any infringement by any officers of the Corora=<span class='line-break'> </span>-tion of the by-law which forbids the Superin=<span class='line-break'> </span>-tendent, Gate-Keeper or other paid servant of the <span class='line-break'> </span>Corporation to have any interest whatever in <span class='line-break'> </span>any work or materials furnished for the Cemetery."</p>
<p>Mess<sup>rs</sup> Norcross, Austin &amp; Cheever were <span class='line-break'> </span>so appointed.<span class='line-break'> </span></p>

<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title=' Trustees _ Nov. 9, 1869 '> Trustees _ <date when='1869-11-09'>Nov. 9, 1869</date> </span></p>
<p>The regular meeting of the Trustees was held<span class='line-break'> </span>on Tuesday <date when='1869-11-09'>November 9, 1869</date>, at 10 'oclock Am.</p>
<p>There were present, the President and Mess<sup>rs</sup><span class='line-break'> </span>Adams, Bowditch Cheever, Livermore, Lovejoy, Norcross,<span class='line-break'> </span>Rand and Read.</p>
<p>The record of the last meeting was read.</p>
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title=' Grading of Coolidge Ave '> Grading of Coolidge Av<sup>e</sup> </span><span class='line-break'> </span>The Committee chosen to authorize the payment<span class='line-break'> </span>of Two hundred and fifty dollars to the City of Cambridge<span class='line-break'> </span>whenver the grading of Coolidge Avenue should be<span class='line-break'> </span>completed to the satisfaction of the Committee, stated,<span class='line-break'> </span></p>
</div>
</div>
<br />
<div id="page-1134321">
<h3><a name="page-1134321">Trustees Records, Vol. 4, 1865 (page 259)</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p>259</p>
<p>that they had received a communication from M<sup>r</sup> Joseph<span class='line-break'> </span>G. Coolidge complaining of the manner in which the City<span class='line-break'> </span>of Cambridge had graded said Avenue in front of his<span class='line-break'> </span>premises.</p>
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title='Treasr authorized to pay $250 for same, upon receiv.g bond of indemnity _'>Treas<sup>r</sup> authorized to pay $250 for same, upon receiv.g bond of indemnity _</span><span class='line-break'> </span>Upon motion of M<sup>r</sup> Rand</p>
<p>Voted. That the Treasurer be authorized to pay $250 ~<span class='line-break'> </span>to the City of Cambridge for the improvements<span class='line-break'> </span>made upon Coolidge Avenue, upon receiving<span class='line-break'> </span>from said City a sufficient bond of indemnity<span class='line-break'> </span>against any claim for damages by the abutters<span class='line-break'> </span>or satisfactory release from said abutters.</p>
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title='Sale of strip of Stone Meadow to City of Camb.'>Sale of strip of Stone Meadow to City of Camb.</span><span class='line-break'> </span>The Committee on Grounds submitted a <span class='line-break'> </span>proposition from the mayor of Cambridge asking speedy<span class='line-break'> </span>action in regard to selling the said City a strip of <span class='line-break'> </span>land next to the Cambridge Cemetery; which was<span class='line-break'> </span>referred back to said Committee with full power.</p>
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title='Appropriation for shrubs &amp; plants _'>Appropriation for shrubs &amp; plants _</span><span class='line-break'> </span>Upon motion of M<sup>r</sup> Rand</p>
<p>Voted. That a sum not exceeding five hundred dollars<span class='line-break'> </span>be expended at the discretion of the Committee<span class='line-break'> </span>on grounds, in the purchase shrubs and<span class='line-break'> </span>plants for the cemetery.</p>
<p>Adjourned for <date when='1869-11-23'>two weeks from this day</date>.</p>
<p>Attest. Austin J. Coolidge</p>
<p>Secretary<span class='line-break'> </span></p>
</div>
</div>

<p>Voted. That the said communication, together with the<span class='line-break'> </span>question whether any change in said form is required,<span class='line-break'> </span>be referred to M<sup>r</sup> Rand to report thereon.<span class='line-break'> </span></p>

<div class="page-content">
<p>265</p>
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title=' Comee to secure fulfilment of Granit Railway Co&apos;, contract _ '> Com<sup>ee</sup> to secure fulfilment of Granit Railway Co', contract _ </span><span class='line-break'> </span>Voted that the same Committee that had charge<span class='line-break'> </span>of the suits of the Granite Railway Company against this<span class='line-break'> </span>Corporation, (Messrs Bigelow, Norcross and Bowditch)<span class='line-break'> </span>be a Committee to see that the agreement of said Granite<span class='line-break'> </span>Railway Company to deliver the remainder of the stones<span class='line-break'> </span>for the Receiving Tomb front on or before the <date when='1870-03-01'>1<sup>st</sup> of<span class='line-break'> </span>March</date> next, is duly Executed.</p>
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title=' Form of Contract for Perpetl Repair _ '> Form of Contract for Perpet<sup>l</sup> Repair _ </span><span class='line-break'> </span>Mr Rand, to whom was referred the communication<span class='line-break'> </span>of A. S. Wheeler Esq. objecting to the present form of<span class='line-break'> </span>contract for the perpetual repair of lots in the Cemetery<span class='line-break'> </span>reported verbally, recommending that a new form of<span class='line-break'> </span>contract for the perpetual repair of lots be substituted<span class='line-break'> </span>for the form now in use, and he submitted a<span class='line-break'> </span>draft of the same. _</p>
<p>After some discussion it was</p>
<p><u>Voted</u> to postpone the consideration of this subject<span class='line-break'> </span>to the next meeting, and that the Secretary send a<span class='line-break'> </span>written copy of the proposed form of contract for per<span class='line-break'></span>petual repair to each member of the Board for his<span class='line-break'> </span>inspection. ~</p>
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title=' Report of Comee relating to classification of Board of Trustees _ '> Report of Com<sup>ee</sup> relating to classification of Board of Trustees _ </span><span class='line-break'> </span>Mr Rand for the Committee appointed to consider<span class='line-break'> </span>and report in what manner the provisions of the<span class='line-break'> </span>last act of the Legislature, relating to the choice of<span class='line-break'> </span>Trustees, should be carried out, submitted the written<span class='line-break'> </span>report of the Committee, which is as follows: _</p>
</div>
</div>
<br />
<div id="page-1134328">
<h3><a name="page-1134328">Trustees Records, Vol. 4, 1865 (page 266)</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p>266</p>
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title=' Trustees _ Decr 14, 1869, contind _ '> Trustees _ <date when='1869-12-14'>Dec<sup>r</sup> 14, 1869</date>, contin<sup>d</sup> _ </span></p>
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title=' Copy of Report of Committee relating to classification of Board of Trustees _ '> Copy of Report of Committee relating to classification of Board of Trustees _ </span><span class='line-break'> </span>"The Committee appointed to consider and report in<span class='line-break'> </span>what manner the provisions of the last Act of the Legis<span class='line-break'></span>lature relating to this Corporation shall be carried<span class='line-break'> </span>into effect" beg leave to report. _</p>
<p>That, in compliance with the third section of the<span class='line-break'> </span>said act, it becomes the duty of the present board<span class='line-break'> </span>of Trustees by lot or otherwise as they themselves may<span class='line-break'> </span>determine to cause the twelve persons who at the time of<span class='line-break'> </span>the passage of the said act constituted the Board of<span class='line-break'> </span>Trustees to be divided into six classes of two each, of whom<span class='line-break'> </span>the persons constituting the first class shall go out of<span class='line-break'> </span>office on the day of the next annual meeting, and<span class='line-break'> </span>the persons of the 2<sup>d</sup>, 3<sup>d</sup>, 4<sup>th</sup>, 5<sup>th</sup>, and 6<sup>th</sup> classes shall go out of<span class='line-break'> </span>office, respectively on the day of each succeeding annual<span class='line-break'> </span>election in the years 1871, 1872, 1873, 1874, and 1875: _<span class='line-break'> </span>that by reason of the vacancy now in the Board by<span class='line-break'> </span>the decease of Mr Chas. C. Little, the provisions of the<span class='line-break'> </span>act will be best complied with by designating one Trustee<span class='line-break'> </span>who shall go out of office on the day of the next annual<span class='line-break'> </span>meeting, and by dividing the rest of the Trustees into five<span class='line-break'> </span>classes of two each.</p>
<p>Your Committee therefore recommend<span class='line-break'> </span>that, unless one Trustee desires to resign, the Trustee who<span class='line-break'> </span>shall go out of office be determined by lot, after which<span class='line-break'> </span>the persons who shall constitute the respective classes<span class='line-break'> </span>be in like manner determined by lot.</p>
<p>They further recommend that the Trustees report<span class='line-break'> </span>to the Proprietors at the annual meeting their doings<span class='line-break'> </span>in this respect, and in what manner the division<span class='line-break'> </span></p>
</div>
</div>
<br />
<div id="page-1134329">
<h3><a name="page-1134329">Trustees Records, Vol. 4, 1865 (page 267)</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p>267</p>
<p>into classes has been made, in order that the<span class='line-break'> </span>Proprietors, in case they shall accept the act, may<span class='line-break'> </span>then proceed to fill the vacancies caused by the decease<span class='line-break'> </span>of Mr Little and the resignation or withdrawal of one<span class='line-break'> </span>other Trustee, pursuant to the terms of the said act.<span class='line-break'> </span><table class='tabular'><thead><span class='line-break'> </span><tr><th>___</th> <th>Edward S. Rand</th> <th>}<span class='line-break'> </span></th></tr></thead> <tbody> <tr><td>___</td> <td>J. Ingersoll Bowditch</td> <td>} Committee</td> </tr> <tr><td>___</td> <td>Edward Austin</td> <td>} " [Committee]</td> </tr> </tbody> </table> <span class='line-break'> </span><span class='depth3' depth='3' title=' Adoption of the foregoing Report _ '> Adoption of the foregoing Report _ </span><span class='line-break'> </span>It was then</p>
<p>Voted that the report be adopted, and that<span class='line-break'> </span>the Board proceed to designate by lot the terms from which<span class='line-break'> </span>the several members of the Board shall serve.</p>
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title=' Term of each member of the Board drawn for by lot _'> Term of each member of the Board drawn for by lot _</span><span class='line-break'> </span>It being determined to regard the vacancy occasioned<span class='line-break'> </span>by the death of Mr Chas. C. Little as one to be filled at<span class='line-break'> </span>the next election by the choice of a new member for<span class='line-break'> </span>the term of six years, one ballot was prepared with the year<span class='line-break'> </span>1870 thereupon, and two each with the years 1871, 1872,<span class='line-break'> </span>1873, 1874 and 1875. _</p>
<p>Mr Bowditch was designated a<span class='line-break'> </span>Committee to superintend the drawing and declare the<span class='line-break'> </span>result. The ballots were closely folded, put into<span class='line-break'> </span>a hat, shaken up, and borne to the Presiden to be<span class='line-break'> </span>drawn out by him. It was agreed that each ballot<span class='line-break'> </span>as drawn should be applied to each trustee in the order<span class='line-break'> </span>in which his name stood on the alphabetical list<span class='line-break'> </span>of Trustees.</p>
</div>

<h3><a name="page-1134331">Trustees Records, Vol. 4, 1865 (page 269)</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p>269</p>
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title=' Trustees _ Decr 28, 1869 '> Trustees _ <date when='1869-12-28'>Dec<sup>r</sup> 28, 1869</date> </span><span class='line-break'> </span>A meeting of the Trustees was held according<span class='line-break'> </span>to adjournment on Tuesday <date when='1869-12-28'>December 28<sup>th</sup> 1869</date>, at<span class='line-break'> </span>10 o'clock a.m. _</p>
<p>There were present, the President, and Messrs.<span class='line-break'> </span>Austin, Bowditch, Cheever, Livermore, Lovejoy, Nor<span class='line-break'></span>cross, Rand, Read and Sleeper. _</p>
<p>The record of the last meeting was read.</p>
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title=' Amendt to By-law relating to Election of Trustees proposed _ '> Amend<sup>t</sup> to By-law relating to Election of Trustees proposed _ </span><span class='line-break'> </span>Mr Rand proposed the following amendment<span class='line-break'> </span>to the By-laws: _</p>
<p>In article 2<sup>d</sup>, substitute for the third<span class='line-break'> </span>sentence, reading _ "The Trustees for the ensuing year<span class='line-break'> </span>shall be elected by ballot _"</p>
<p>the words _</p>
<p>"The vacancies<span class='line-break'> </span>in the Board of Trustees caused by death, resignation<span class='line-break'> </span>or by the expiration of the term for which any Trustees were<span class='line-break'> </span>elected shall be filled by ballot."</p>
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title=' Form of contract for perpetual repair of Lots _ '> Form of contract for perpetual repair of Lots _ </span><span class='line-break'> </span>Voted to take from table the form of con<span class='line-break'></span>tract proposed by Mr Read at the last meeting,<span class='line-break'> </span>to be used for guaranteeing the perpetual repair of lots.</p>
<p>Mr Livermore moved that the form of contract<span class='line-break'> </span>submitted by Mr Rand be adopted.</p>
<p>After a lengthy discussion the motion was<span class='line-break'> </span>adopted. _</p>
</div>

<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title=' Amendt of art. 7 _ Superintendt proposed _ '> Amend<sup>t</sup> of art. 7 _ Superintend<sup>t</sup> proposed _ </span><span class='line-break'> </span>Mr Rand proposed as an amendment to<span class='line-break'> </span>Article 7 of the By-laws the following additional<span class='line-break'> </span>clause at the end of the article: _</p>

<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title=' Trustees _ Jany. 11, 1870 _ continued _ '> Trustees _ <date when='1870-01-11'>Jany. 11, 1870</date> _ continued _ </span><span class='line-break'> </span>report thereon _ with instructions also to<span class='line-break'> </span>report what change, if any, is necessary, in<span class='line-break'> </span>the By, law relating to the Repair Fund. _</p>
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title=' Amendt to Art. 7 _ Superintendt _  proposed in new form.'> Amend<sup>t</sup> to Art. 7 _ Superintend<sup>t</sup> _  proposed in new form.</span><span class='line-break'> </span>The amendment proposed by Mr<span class='line-break'> </span>Rand, at the last meeting, to article 7, was<span class='line-break'> </span>taken from the table.</p>
<p>After discussion, the Amendment as originally offered<span class='line-break'> </span>was withdrawn, and an Amendment to said article<span class='line-break'> </span>was offered in form as follows: _</p>
<p>"He shall not <span class='line-break'> </span>receive from any proprietor, or contractor for work or<span class='line-break'> </span>materials, any commission or fees, or any compensation<span class='line-break'> </span>for any services rendered by him, except as herein<span class='line-break'> </span>after provided: the Superintendent shall be allowed<span class='line-break'> </span>to render special services in the laying out and<span class='line-break'> </span>ornamentation of any lot upon the request of the<span class='line-break'> </span>proprietor thereof, such proprietor first obtaining a<span class='line-break'> </span>permit in writing from the Secretary, and the Superintendent<span class='line-break'> </span>shall be allowed to charge such compensation for the<span class='line-break'> </span>services so rendered as the Committee on Lots shall<span class='line-break'> </span>approve, and shall, once in six months, render to the<span class='line-break'> </span>Trustees an account in detail of the sums so received." _</p>
<p>Voted that when this meeting shall be adjourned, it <span class='line-break'> </span>be to <date when='1870-01-18'>this day one week</date>, at ten o'clock a.m _<span class='line-break'> </span><table class='tabular'><thead><span class='line-break'> </span><tr><th>___</th> <th>Adjourned<span class='line-break'> </span></th></tr></thead> <tbody> <tr><td>___</td> <td>___</td> <td>Attest Austin J. Coolidge Sec.y</td> </tr> </tbody> </table></p>

<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title=' Trustees - Jan.y 18, 1870. '> Trustees - <date when='1870-01-18'>Jan.y 18, 1870</date>. </span><span class='line-break'> </span>A meeting of the Trustees was held according to<span class='line-break'> </span>adjournment on Tuesday, <date when='1870-01-18'>January 18<sup>th</sup> 1870</date>, at<span class='line-break'> </span>ten o'clock a.m _</p>

<p>The record of the last meeting was read. _</p>
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title=' Form of contract for Perpetual Repair of Lots adopted _'> Form of contract for Perpetual Repair of Lots adopted _</span><span class='line-break'> </span>The Committee on Lots reported back the<span class='line-break'> </span>form of contract for perpetual repair of lots re<span class='line-break'></span>ferred to them at the last meeting, recommending<span class='line-break'> </span>that it be adopted in the form first reported, with the<span class='line-break'> </span>addition of a clause requiring a special vote of the<span class='line-break'> </span>Board of Trustees, before using any portion of the<span class='line-break'> </span>surplus income of the Repair Fund for ornamenting<span class='line-break'> </span>and preserving the grounds of the Cemetery.</p>
<p>Voted to accept the report, and that the<span class='line-break'> </span>form of contract for the perpetual repair of lots, as<span class='line-break'> </span>now presented, be adopted and hereafter used _ <span class='line-break'> </span>the same being in form as follows: _</p>

<p>Mr Cheever moved to strike out from said<span class='line-break'> </span>proposed amendment all after the words _<span class='line-break'> </span>"rendered by him": but the motion was rejected. _</p>
<p>Mr Rand moved the adoption of the proposed<span class='line-break'> </span>amendment.</p>
<p>Mr Cheever called for the yeas and nays _</p>
<p>Upon the question being taken, _</p>
<p>Messrs Adams, Austin, Bigelow, Bowditch, Liv<span class='line-break'></span>ermore, Norcross, Rand and Read, voted yea _<span class='line-break'> </span>and Mr Cheever " [voted] nay. _</p>
<p>And the Amendment as proposed was<span class='line-break'> </span>declared to be adopted as a part of By-law article<span class='line-break'> </span>seven. ~<span class='line-break'> </span><table class='tabular'><thead><span class='line-break'> </span><tr><th>___</th> <th>Adjourned<span class='line-break'> </span></th></tr></thead> <tbody> <tr><td>___</td> <td>___</td> <td>Attest, Austin J. <p>282</p>
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title=' Proprietors&apos; Annual Meeting _ February 7. 1870 _'> Proprietors' Annual Meeting _ <date when='1870-02-07'>February 7. 1870</date> _</span><span class='line-break'> </span>Proprietors' Annual Meeting<span class='line-break'> </span>Monday, <date when='1870-02-07'>February 7, 1870</date>.</p>
<p>------------------</p>
<p>In accordance with the notice prescribed in the<span class='line-break'> </span>amended charter (a copy whereof is hereto annexed)<span class='line-break'> </span>served upon the members of the Corporation and<span class='line-break'> </span>published in one or more of the Boston newspapers,<span class='line-break'> </span>the Proprietors met at Horticultural Hall,<span class='line-break'> </span>Boston, on Monday, <date when='1870-02-07'>February 7<sup>th</sup></date> at 3½ o'clock,<span class='line-break'> </span>P.m.</p>
<p>A quorum being in attendance, the President,<span class='line-break'> </span>Dr Jacob Bigelow, took the chair. _</p>
<p>The Secretary red the call for the meeting, and<span class='line-break'> </span>the records of the last annual meeting.</p>
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title=' Trustees&apos; Annual Report _'> Trustees' Annual Report _</span><span class='line-break'> </span>The Annual Report of the Trustees was<span class='line-break'> </span>also read by the Secretary. ~</p>
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title=' Motion to accept Report of Trustees tabled _ '> Motion to accept Report of Trustees tabled _ </span><span class='line-break'> </span>Mr Alfred T. Turner moved to accept<span class='line-break'> </span>the Report of the Trustees. _</p>
<p>Mr John R. Poor moved that the motion<span class='line-break'> </span>to accept the Report of the Trustees lie upon<span class='line-break'> </span>the table, _ which motion was adopted. _</p>
</div>

<div id="page-1134345">
<h3><a name="page-1134345">Trustees Records, Vol. 4, 1865 (page 283)</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p>283</p>
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title=' Motion to Annual Amendt to Art. 7 of By-Laws _ recently adopted by Trustees _ '> Motion to Annual Amend<sup>t</sup> to Art. 7 of By-Laws _ recently adopted by Trustees _ </span><span class='line-break'> </span>Mr A. T. Turner moved the adoption of<span class='line-break'> </span>the following order: _</p>
<p>Whereas, at a meeting of<span class='line-break'> </span>the Proprietors of the Cemetery of Mount Auburn,<span class='line-break'> </span>held <date when='1835-07-10'>July 10, 1835</date>, the following vote or by-law<span class='line-break'> </span>was adopted, viz.</p>
<p>'Third _ The Trustees shall have<span class='line-break'> </span>authority to make any by-laws for the due regulation<span class='line-break'> </span>and management of the property, business and<span class='line-break'> </span>prudential concerns of the Corporation, not other<span class='line-break'></span>wise provided for by the act of incorporation, which<span class='line-break'> </span>shall be in force till otherwise ordered by the<span class='line-break'> </span>Corporation ' _</p>
<p>It is hereby ordered that so much of<span class='line-break'> </span>the Amendment to By-Laws Art. 7 which was passed<span class='line-break'> </span>by the Trustees <date when='1870-01-11'>January 11, 1870</date> as is comprised in<span class='line-break'> </span>the following words,</p>
<p>"Except as hereinafter provided: the<span class='line-break'> </span>Superintendent shall be allowed to render special services in the laying<span class='line-break'> </span>out and ornamentation of any lot, upon the request of the propri<span class='line-break'></span>etor thereof, such proprietor first obtaining a permit in writing<span class='line-break'> </span>from the Secretary; and the Superintendent shall be allowed<span class='line-break'> </span>to charge such compensation for the services so rendered<span class='line-break'> </span>as the Committee on Lots shall approve; and shall,<span class='line-break'> </span>once in six months, render to the Trustees an account<span class='line-break'> </span>in detail of the sums so received" _</p>
<p>be and the<span class='line-break'> </span>same hereby is declared null and void and<span class='line-break'> </span>not in force; and so much of said By-law</p>
</div>
</div>
<br />
<div id="page-1134346">
<h3><a name="page-1134346">Trustees Records, Vol. 4, 1865 (page 284)</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p>284</p>
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title=' Feb.y 7, 1870. '> <date when='1870-02-07'>Feb.y 7, 1870</date>. </span><span class='line-break'> </span>[Proprietors' Annual Meeting]</p>
<p>as is comprised in the following words,</p>
<p>"He<span class='line-break'> </span>shall not receive from any proprietor, or contractor for work<span class='line-break'> </span>or materials, any commission, or fees, or any compensa<span class='line-break'></span>tion for any services rendered by him," -</p>
<p>is hereby<span class='line-break'> </span>approved; and nothing contained in<span class='line-break'> </span>Article 3<sup>d</sup> of the By-Laws shall be so construed<span class='line-break'> </span>as to conflict with or set aside so much of<span class='line-break'> </span>said amendment of the By-laws as is<span class='line-break'> </span>hereby adopted and approved.</p>
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title=' Committee of five chosen to consider subject of Amendt to Art. 7 of By-Laws and report at adjourned meeting _ '> Committee of five chosen to consider subject of Amend<sup>t</sup> to Art. 7 of By-Laws and report at adjourned meeting _ </span><span class='line-break'> </span>Pending the consideration of the aforesaid<span class='line-break'> </span>order,</p>
<p>Mr John R. Poor moved</p>
<p>That a Committee<span class='line-break'> </span>of five be appointed to take the subject of<span class='line-break'> </span>the Amendment to By-Laws Article 7 into con<span class='line-break'></span>sideration and report thereon at a meeting<span class='line-break'> </span>to which this meeting shall be adjourned. _</p>
<p>The motion for commitment being first in order,<span class='line-break'> </span>was put and adopted. _</p>
<p>Upon motion by Mr Jess Halbrook, it was</p>
<p>Voted that the Committee be chosen<span class='line-break'> </span>by nomination at large;</p>
<p>Under which,<span class='line-break'> </span></p>
</div>
</div>

<p>----------</p>
<p>The Proprietors of the Cemetery of Mount Auburn<span class='line-break'> </span>met according to adjournment _ notice of said meeting<span class='line-break'> </span>having been given in the manner directed. _ at<span class='line-break'> </span>the Horticultural Hall, Tremont Street, Boston,<span class='line-break'> </span>on Monday, <date when='1870-03-07'>March 7, 1870</date>, at half past three<span class='line-break'> </span>o'clock P.m.</p>
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title=' President calls to order _ vacates the Chair _ Mr Otis Norcross chosen Chairman _'> President calls to order _ vacates the Chair _ Mr Otis Norcross chosen Chairman _</span><span class='line-break'> </span>A quorum being in attendance, the President,<span class='line-break'> </span>Dr. Jacob Bigelow took the chair, and stated, that<span class='line-break'> </span>as he should be unable to attend during the whole<span class='line-break'> </span>meeting, he would nominate to the chair,</p>
<p>Mr Otis Norcross,</p>
<p>The motion was put, and declared adopted, and<span class='line-break'> </span>Mr Norcross took the chair.</p>
<p>The Secretary read the record of the previous meeting<span class='line-break'> </span>on the <date when='1870-02-07'>7<sup>th</sup> of February</date>. ~</p>

<p>Mr Poor the chairman read the report of the<span class='line-break'> </span>Committee, which was accompanied with the following<span class='line-break'> </span>recommendations _</p>
<p>On page 8 _ "We therefore recommend the Trustees<span class='line-break'> </span>to allow the proprietors the full advantage of all<span class='line-break'> </span></p>

<div id="page-1134349">
<h3><a name="page-1134349">Trustees Records, Vol. 4, 1865 (page 287)</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p>287</p>
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title=' Amendments proposed _ to By-Laws _ Art. 3, and Art. 7. '> Amendments proposed _ to By-Laws _ Art. 3, and Art. 7. </span><span class='line-break'> </span>discounts made upon materials."</p>
<p>Page 9 - "We therefore recommend our Board of<span class='line-break'> </span>Trustees to recall their amendment to Article 7 of<span class='line-break'> </span>the By-laws passed by their <date when='1870-01-11'>January 11, 1870</date>, and<span class='line-break'> </span>to substitute therefor the following changes in the<span class='line-break'> </span>By-Laws.</p>
<p>1<sup>st</sup> Amending Article 3<sup>d</sup>, so that it shall read,<span class='line-break'> </span>after the word "Trustee," in the third line of the last clause: _</p>
<p>"And neither the Superintendent, Gate Keeper, nor<span class='line-break'> </span>any paid servant of the Corporation shall have any<span class='line-break'> </span>interest in, or receive any compensation whatever,<span class='line-break'> </span>direct or indirect for any work designed for the Ceme<span class='line-break'></span>tery or for any lot or lots therein, or for materials<span class='line-break'> </span>furnished for the same in any manner whatsoever:" _<span class='line-break'> </span>and</p>
<p>Amending Article 7, by adding after the word<span class='line-break'> </span>"perquisites",</p>
<p>"And he shall not receive from any pro<span class='line-break'></span>prietor, or contractor for work or material any com<span class='line-break'></span>mission, fees, presents, or any compensation direct<span class='line-break'> </span>or indirect, for any services rendered by him, and<span class='line-break'> </span>nothing contained in any other article of the By-laws<span class='line-break'> </span>shall be construed as to conflict with or set<span class='line-break'> </span>aside these restrictions."</p>
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title=' Report accepted &amp; Recommendations adopted. '> Report accepted &amp; Recommendations adopted. </span><span class='line-break'> </span>On motion by Mr. A. T. Turner it was</p>
<p>Voted that the report be accepted and the<span class='line-break'> </span>recommendations adopted. _<span class='line-break'> </span></p>

<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title=' Rev. G.E. Ellis declined to run as candidate _ '> Rev. G.E. Ellis declined to run as candidate _ </span><span class='line-break'> </span>Rev<sup>d</sup> Geo. E. Ellis said that he had been informed<span class='line-break'> </span>since he entered the hall that his name had been<span class='line-break'> </span>placed upon on of the ballots as a candidate for the<span class='line-break'> </span>Board of Trustees. It had been so used without his <span class='line-break'> </span>knowledge or consent, and as it would be impos<span class='line-break'></span>sible for him to serve, he must respectfully decline<span class='line-break'> </span>the nomination.</p>

<div id="page-1134354">
<h3><a name="page-1134354">Trustees Records, Vol. 4, 1865 (page 292)</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p>292</p>
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title=' Trustee&apos;s Annual Report. '> Trustee's Annual Report. </span><span class='line-break'> </span><u>Trustee's Report.</u></p>
<p>At the Annual Meeting of the Proprietors of the Cemetery<span class='line-break'> </span>of Mount Auburn, holden in Boston, <date when='1869-02-01'>February 1, 1869</date>, measures<span class='line-break'> </span>were taken to cause a petition to be presented to the Legis<span class='line-break'></span>lature of the Commonwealth, asking for amendments in<span class='line-break'> </span>the Charter of this Corporation relating to the election of<span class='line-break'> </span>Trustees, and to certain other matters.</p>
<p>In pursuance of votes taken at different times by this<span class='line-break'> </span>Corporation, a petition has been duly presented to the<span class='line-break'> </span>Legislature, and an Act has been passed by them, of which<span class='line-break'> </span>a copy is here subjoined: _</p>
<p>An Act in addition to an Act to Incorporate the Proprie<span class='line-break'></span>tors of the Cemetery of Mount Auburn.</p>
<p>Be it enacted by the Senate and House of Representatives<span class='line-break'> </span>in General Court assembled and by the authority of the same<span class='line-break'> </span>as follows:</p>
<p><u>Section 1.</u> The authority conferred upon any cemetery corp<span class='line-break'></span>ration organized under the provisions of Section two of<span class='line-break'> </span>Chapter twenty-eight of the General Statutes, to take and<span class='line-break'> </span>hold so much real and personal estate as may be necessary<span class='line-break'> </span>for the objects of its organization, is hereby vested in the<span class='line-break'> </span>Proprietors of the Cemetery of Mount Auburn.</p>
<p><u>Sect.2.</u> No member of the said Corporation shall, in his in<span class='line-break'></span>dividual right, be entitled to more than one vote at the<span class='line-break'> </span>meetings of said Corporation.</p>
<p><u>Sect.3.</u> The officers of the said Corporation shall consist of<span class='line-break'> </span>twelve Trustees, a Treasurer, Secretary, and such other offi<span class='line-break'></span>cers as the Trustees shall direct. The twelve persons who now<span class='line-break'> </span></p>
</div>
</div>
<br />
<div id="page-1134355">
<h3><a name="page-1134355">Trustees Records, Vol. 4, 1865 (page 293)</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p>293</p>
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title=' Trustee&apos;s Annual Report. '> Trustee's Annual Report. </span><span class='line-break'> </span>constitute the Board of Trustees shall be divided by lot, or<span class='line-break'> </span>otherwise, as they themselves may determine, into six classes<span class='line-break'> </span>of two each; and the persons of the first class shall go out of<span class='line-break'> </span>office on the day of the next annual meeting; and the<span class='line-break'> </span>persons of the second, third, fourth, fifth, and sixth classes<span class='line-break'> </span>shall go out of office, respectively, on the day of each suc<span class='line-break'></span>ceeding annual election in the years eighteen hundred<span class='line-break'> </span>seventy-one, eighteen hundred seventy-two, eighteen hun<span class='line-break'></span>dred seventy-three, eighteen hundred seventy four and<span class='line-break'> </span>eighteen hundred seventy five; and the two Trustees who<span class='line-break'> </span>shall be chosen at the annual meeting in the year eight<span class='line-break'></span>een hundred and seventy, and in each succeeding year,<span class='line-break'> </span>shall continue in office, respectively for the term of six<span class='line-break'> </span>years. In case of the death or resignation of any Trustee,<span class='line-break'> </span>the vacancy shall be filled by the Proprietors at the next<span class='line-break'> </span>annual meeting succeeding such death or resignation.</p>
<p>Nothing herein contained shall prevent any person<span class='line-break'> </span>whose term of office shall have expired from being re<span class='line-break'></span>eligible.</p>
<p><u>Sect. 4.</u> The Secretary shall give notice of annual<span class='line-break'> </span>and special meetings of said Corporation by sending by mail<span class='line-break'> </span>or otherwise, to each member of the Corporation whose place<span class='line-break'> </span>of residence or business shall be known to him, a printed<span class='line-break'> </span>notice thereof seven days before the time of such meeting, and<span class='line-break'> </span>by publication of such notice in one or more newspapers<span class='line-break'> </span>printed in Boston, seven days before the time of such<span class='line-break'> </span>meeting. At all meetings a quorum for business shall<span class='line-break'> </span>consist of not less than twenty-five members.<span class='line-break'> </span></p>
</div>
</div>
<br />
<div id="page-1134356">
<h3><a name="page-1134356">Trustees Records, Vol. 4, 1865 (page 294)</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p>294</p>
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title=' Trustee&apos;s Annual Report. '> Trustee's Annual Report. </span><span class='line-break'> </span><u>Sect. 5.</u> Such parts of Sections two, three, four, and five of<span class='line-break'> </span>Chapter ninety-six of the Acts of the year<date when='1835'> eighteen hundred <span class='line-break'> </span>and thirty five</date>, or of any Act in addition thereto, which may<span class='line-break'> </span>be inconsistent with the provisions of this Act, are hereby<span class='line-break'> </span>repealed.</p>
<p>Approved <date when='1869-04-17'>April 17, 1869</date>.</p>
<p>In compliance with the foregoing Act of the Legislature,<span class='line-break'> </span>the Trustees at their meeting held <date when='1869-12-14'>December 14, 1869</date>, voted,<span class='line-break'> </span>to proceed to divide their board into six classes, and to<span class='line-break'> </span>decide, by lot at what time the period of service of each<span class='line-break'> </span>of the present incumbents should expire. The lots being<span class='line-break'> </span>drawn, the result was declared as follows, (the name of<span class='line-break'> </span>Mr. Charles C. Little, deceased, being omitted,) _<span class='line-break'> </span>To go out of office at the Annual Meeting<span class='line-break'> </span><table class='tabular'><thead><span class='line-break'> </span><tr><th>___</th> <th>1870,</th> <th>James Read.<span class='line-break'> </span></th></tr></thead> <tbody> <tr><td>___</td> <td>1871,</td> <td>{ Paul Adams,</td> </tr> <tr><td>___</td> <td>___</td> <td>{ Edward S. Rand.</td> </tr> <tr><td>___</td> <td>1872,</td> <td>{ J. Ingersoll Bowditch,</td> </tr> <tr><td>___</td> <td>___</td> <td>{ Loyal Lovejoy.</td> </tr> <tr><td>___</td> <td>1873,</td> <td>{ Edward Austin,</td> </tr> <tr><td>___</td> <td>___</td> <td>{ Jacob Bigelow.</td> </tr> <tr><td>___</td> <td>1874,</td> <td>{ Isaac Livermore,</td> </tr> <tr><td>___</td> <td>___</td> <td>{ Jacob Sleeper.</td> </tr> <tr><td>___</td> <td>1875,</td> <td>{ James Cheever,</td> </tr> <tr><td>___</td> <td>___</td> <td>{ Otis Norcross.</td> </tr> </tbody> </table> <span class='line-break'> </span>During the past year many trees, constituting nearly<span class='line-break'> </span>half the whole number standing at the beginning of the<span class='line-break'> </span>year, have been culled out and removed, greatly improving<span class='line-break'> </span></p>
